<div class="ra xbox p" role="complementary" aria-label="Related or updated information about this article"><div>The publisher's version of this article is available at <a href="https://doi.org/10.1002/cpmc.129" class="usa-link usa-link--external" data-ga-action="click_feat_suppl" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Curr Protoc Microbiol</a>
</div></div>
</div></section></section><section aria-label="Article content"><section class="body main-article-body"><section class="abstract" id="ABS1"><h2>Abstract</h2>
<p id="P2">Human papillomavirus (HPV) infection occurs in differentiating epithelial tissues, and cancers caused by the high-risk types (e.g., HPV16 and HPV18) typically occur at oropharyngeal and anogenital anatomical sites. The HPV life cycle is differentiation-dependent, requiring tissue culture methodology able to recapitulate the three-dimensional (3D) stratified epithelium. Here we report two distinct and complementary methods to grow differentiating epithelial tissues that mimic many critical morphological and biochemical aspects of <em>in vivo</em> tissue. The first approach involves growing primary human epithelial cells on top of a dermal equivalent consisting of collagen fibers and living fibroblast cells. When these cells are grown at the liquid-air interface, differentiation occurs and allows for epithelial stratification. The second approach uses a rotating wall vessel (RWV) bioreactor. The low-fluid-shear microgravity environment inside the bioreactor allows the cells to use collagen-coated microbeads as a growth scaffold and self assemble into 3D cellular aggregates. These approaches are applied to epithelial cells derived from HPV-positive and -negative oral and cervical tissues. The second part of the protocol introduces potential downstream applications for these 3D tissue models.</p>
<p id="P3">We describe methods that will allow readers to start successfully culturing 3D tissues from oral and cervical cells. These tissues have been used for microscopic visualization, scanning-electron microscopy, and large -omics studies to gain insights into epithelial biology, the HPV life cycle, and host-pathogen interactions.</p>
<p id="P4">Support Protocol 1: Isolation of epithelial cells from patient-derived tissues</p>
<p id="P5">Support Protocol 2: Growth and maintenance of primary human epithelial cells in monolayer culture</p>
<p id="P6">Support Protocol 3: PCR-based HPV screening of primary cell cultures</p>
<p id="P7">Basic Protocol 1: Establishing human primary cell-derived 3D organotypic raft cultures</p>
<p id="P8">Support Protocol 4: Growth and maintenance of human A2EN cells as monolayer culture</p>
<p id="P9">Support Protocol 5: Preparing the slow turning lateral vessel bioreactor</p>
<p id="P10">Support Protocol 6: Preparing the cytodex-3 microcarrier beads</p>
<p id="P11">Basic Protocol 2: Establishing human 3D cervical tissues using the rotating wall vessel bioreactor</p>
<p id="P12">Basic Protocol 3: Histological assessment of 3D organotypic raft tissues</p>
<p id="P13">Basic Protocol 4: Spatial analysis of protein expression in 3D organotypic raft cultures</p>
<p id="P14">Basic Protocol 5: Immunofluorescent microscopy imaging of rotating wall vessel derived 3D tissues</p>
<p id="P15">Basic Protocol 6: Ultrastructural visualization and imaging of rotating wall vessel derived 3D tissues</p>
<p id="P16">Support Protocol 7: RNA extraction from 3D tissues</p>
<p id="P17">Basic Protocol 7: Characterization of gene expression by RT-qPCR</p>
<section id="kwd-group1" class="kwd-group"><p><strong>Keywords:</strong> HPV, organotypic rafts, rotating wall vessel, bioreactor, 3D culture, cervix, oral, host-microbe interactions</p></section></section><section id="S1"><h2 class="pmc_sec_title">INTRODUCTION</h2>
<p id="P18">Papillomaviruses are a diverse family of double-stranded DNA viruses with an epithelial tropism, infecting both cutaneous and mucosal epithelia of vertebrate hosts, including humans. Human papillomaviruses (HPVs) are ubiquitous infectious agents in human populations (<a href="#R63" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R63">Schiffman et al., 2016</a>) and the most common sexually transmitted pathogen (<a href="#R62" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R62">Satterwhite et al., 2013</a>). Oncogenic HPV infections are responsible for a staggering ~5% of human cancers (<a href="#R14" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R14">de Martel et al., 2020</a>; <a href="#R73" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R73">Zapatka et al., 2020</a>). In addition to being responsible for virtually all cervical cancers, the incidence of HPV-associated oral cancers has dramatically increased during recent years (<a href="#R12" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R12">Chaturvedi et al., 2011</a>; <a href="#R45" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R45">Marur et al., 2010</a>), making oropharyngeal squamous cell carcinoma (OPSCC) the most common HPV-related malignancy in the United States (<a href="#R21" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R21">Eisenberg et al., 2018</a>). Of note, most HPV-positive OPSCCs arise in the tonsil crypts.</p>
<p id="P19">Following the initial infection of basal cells, the HPV DNA is amplified and established as a low copy number extrachromosomal genome. Within these actively dividing cells, the HPV genome replicates alongside the host genome. As part of the cellular differentiation cycle, infected cells detach from the basement membrane and enter the suprabasal epithelial layer. Unlike uninfected cells, the expression of the viral E6 (<a href="#R19" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R19">Duffy et al., 2003</a>; <a href="#R37" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R37">Kranjec et al., 2017</a>; <a href="#R49" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R49">Morgan et al., 2018</a>) and E7 (<a href="#R6" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R6">Bodily et al., 2011</a>; <a href="#R23" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R23">Flores et al., 2000</a>; <a href="#R50" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R50">Müller et al., 1999</a>) proteins promotes unscheduled cell cycle progression, supporting continuous viral replication. As the cells continue to differentiate, increased expression of the E1 and E2 replication proteins leads to a transition towards productive viral DNA amplification (<a href="#R61" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R61">Sakakibara et al., 2013</a>). Finally, within the terminally differentiated layers of the epithelium, the viral capsid proteins (L1, <a href="#R7" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R7">Buck et al., 2013</a>); and L2, <a href="#R70" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R70">Wang &amp; Roden, 2013</a>) are synthesized, leading to virion assembly. This synchronized gene expression implies that the completion of the viral life cycle requires the three-dimensional stratified epithelium.</p>
<p id="P20">Keratinocytes in the different strata of the differentiated tissue must coordinate their gene expression to fulfill specific and dynamic functions during cellular differentiation. At the stratum level, expression of many of the cellular genes are known, but how spatio-temporal gene expression is regulated is a topic of intense investigation (<a href="#R9" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R9">Cavazza et al., 2016</a>; <a href="#R22" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R22">Finnegan et al., 2019</a>; <a href="#R34" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R34">Joost et al., 2016</a>; <a href="#R35" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R35">Klein et al., 2017</a>; <a href="#R43" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R43">Lopez-Pajares et al., 2015</a>; <a href="#R59" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R59">Rubin et al., 2019</a>). Modeling the physiologically relevant tissues will be critical to further our understanding of the viral life cycle.</p>
<p id="P21">The methods described in this protocol will outline two distinct and complementary approaches to reliably and reproducibly generate and characterize 3D tissues. By modeling the complexity of the full-thickness epithelium, these culture methods address a significant limitation of two-dimensional monolayer cultures. These culture models have been shown to faithfully recapitulate many morphological and physiological characteristics of tissue <em>in vivo</em>. These cultures not only preserve the cellular architecture of the cervical or tonsillar tissue but also respond to external stimuli in ways that mimic the response in the <em>in vivo</em> microenvironment (<a href="#R2" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R2">Asselineau &amp; Prunieras, 1984</a>; <a href="#R36" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R36">Kopan et al., 1987</a>; <a href="#R55" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R55">Radtke et al., 2012</a>; <a href="#R54" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R54">Radtke &amp; Herbst-Kralovetz, 2012</a>).</p>
<p id="P22">We provide methods to successfully isolate oral and cervical cells from donor-derived tissues, grow these cells into 3D epithelial tissues, and characterize them through a series of microscopic (histological, scanning electron microscopy, and immunofluorescence) and transcriptome-based analyses (<a href="#F1" class="usa-link">Fig. 1</a>). Support Protocol 1 describes the isolation of primary epithelial cells (keratinocytes) from patient-derived tissues (e.g., cervical biopsies and tonsillectomies). These primary cultures are maintained as monolayers in <a href="#S8" class="usa-link">Support Protocol 2</a> and screened for HPV DNA by PCR in <a href="#S13" class="usa-link">Support Protocol 3</a>. <a href="#S22" class="usa-link">Basic Protocols 1</a> and <a href="#S49" class="usa-link">2</a> describe two distinct methods to generate 3D cultures: organotypic rafting or rotating wall vessel bioreactor. Cells and materials for Basic Protocol 2 are prepared using Support Protocol 4 (to grow and maintain cells) as well as Support Protocols 5 and 6 (to prepare the bioreactor and carrier beads used). An array of host differentiation and viral life cycle characterization techniques are detailed in <a href="#S54" class="usa-link">Basic Protocol 3</a> (histology), Basic Protocols 3 and 4 (immunofluorescence for raft tissues or rotating wall vessel tissues, respectively), Basic Protocol 6 (electron microscopy), and Support Protocol 7 (RNA extraction) coupled with Basic Protocol 7 (RT-qPCR).</p>
<figure class="fig xbox font-sm" id="F1"><h3 class="obj_head">Figure 1.</h3>
<p class="img-box line-height-none margin-x-neg-2 tablet:margin-x-0 text-center"><img class="graphic" src="https://cdn.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/blobs/3a7a/11088941/a8763aae7b17/nihms-1991549-f0001.jpg" loading="lazy" height="1164" width="1920" alt="Figure 1"></p>
<div class="p text-right font-secondary"><a href="figure/F1/" class="usa-link" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Open in a new tab</a></div>
<figcaption><p id="P785">Flowchart of all protocols described in this protocol for preparing, culturing, and characterizing 3D oral and cervical tissue models for studying interactions between HPV and the infected host. The dotted line connecting Support Protocol 1 to Basic Protocol 2 indicates that, with proper optimization, it should be feasible to culture primary cells in the Rotating wall vessel bioreactor.</p></figcaption></figure><section id="S2"><h3 class="pmc_sec_title">Biosafety and ethics considerations</h3>
<p id="P23"><em>CAUTION</em>: Human tissues, cells, and HPV virions are a potential biohazard. Laboratory personnel should follow all biosafety and ethical guidelines relevant to local facilities, institutions, and governing bodies to properly acquire and handle donor-derived human samples that may contain pathogenic microorganisms. Appropriately trained individuals should conduct all work in accordance with your local guidelines and regulations. Human papillomavirus is considered a biosafety level 2 (BSL-2) pathogen (<a href="#R20" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R20">Dunne et al., 2014</a>; <em>Human Papillomavirus Vaccination: Recommendations of the Advisory Committee on Immunization Practices (ACIP)</em>) and since 3D raft cultures are capable of producing infectious viral particles within the superficial layer (as virus-laden squames), BSL-2 precautions (e.g., personal protective equipment and using a biosafety cabinet) must be taken while handling cultures. In addition to good laboratory practice and aseptic technique, these precautions ensure reader safety and preserve the quality of results by limiting contamination.</p></section></section><section id="S3"><h2 class="pmc_sec_title">
<em>SUPPORT PROTOCOL 1:</em> Isolation of epithelial cells from patient derived tissues</h2>
<p id="P24">Keratinocytes are the predominant cell type that comprises stratified epithelia and can be isolated directly from patient-derived donor tissues from anatomic sites (e.g., oral and cervical epithelia) relevant to the HPV life cycle. This protocol provides detailed steps to isolate these primary cells from donor specific tissues. These tissues should be isolated by qualified medical personnel in accordance with institutional and Federal human protection guidelines. Tissues and isolated cell lines are a biosafety level 2 pathogen and should be handled accordingly. As an alternative, primary keratinocytes are available commercially.</p>
<section id="S4"><h3 class="pmc_sec_title">Materials</h3>
<section id="S5"><h4 class="pmc_sec_title">Reagents, solutions, and cell lines</h4>
<ul id="L2" class="list" style="list-style-type:none">
<li><p id="P25">Donor tissue specimens collected by qualified personnel</p></li>
<li><p id="P26">Transport media (see recipe)</p></li>
<li><p id="P27">Dulbecco’s phosphate-buffered saline (D-PBS; ThermoFisher Scientific, cat. no. 14190–144)</p></li>
<li><p id="P28">10% buffered formalin (Fisher Scientific, cat. no. SF98–4)</p></li>
<li>
<p id="P29">Penicillin and streptomycin (ThermoFisher Scientific, cat. no. 15140122)</p>
<p id="P30">Amphotericin B (Sigma-Aldrich, cat. no. A2411–250MG)</p>
</li>
<li><p id="P31">Dispase II, working concentration 2.4 U/ml in HBSS (Sigma-Aldrich, cat. no. D4693–1G)</p></li>
<li><p id="P32">0.25% trypsin/EDTA (ThermoFisher Scientific, cat. no. 25200056)</p></li>
<li><p id="P33">Inactivation media (see recipe)0.4% Trypan blue (VWR, cat. no. 97063–702)</p></li>
<li><p id="P34">Rheinwald-Green medium (F-media; see recipe)</p></li>
<li><p id="P35">Terminally Irradiated (6000 Rad) 3T3-Swiss albino J2 mouse embryonic fibroblasts (see Current Protocols article: <a href="#R66" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R66">Takashima, 2001</a>)</p></li>
</ul></section><section id="S6"><h4 class="pmc_sec_title">Hardware and instruments</h4>
<ul id="L4" class="list" style="list-style-type:none">
<li><p id="P36">50 ml conical tubes</p></li>
<li><p id="P37">4°C fridge</p></li>
<li><p id="P38">1.5 ml microcentrifuge tubes</p></li>
<li><p id="P39">Scalpel and sterile blades</p></li>
<li><p id="P40">Autoclave sterilizer</p></li>
<li><p id="P41">Sterile forceps</p></li>
<li><p id="P42">−80°C freezer</p></li>
<li><p id="P43">6-well plate</p></li>
<li><p id="P44">70 μm cell strainer (Corning, cat. no. 352350)</p></li>
<li><p id="P45">Automated cell counter and counting slides</p></li>
<li><p id="P46">Centrifuge</p></li>
<li><p id="P47">10 cm tissue culture plates (USA Scientific, cat. no. CC7682–3394)</p></li>
<li><p id="P48">Humidified 5% CO<sub>2</sub> incubator</p></li>
<li><p id="P49">Humidified 10% CO<sub>2</sub> incubator</p></li>
<li><p id="P50">Liquid nitrogen tank</p></li>
</ul></section></section><section id="S7"><h3 class="pmc_sec_title">Protocol steps</h3>
<ol id="L6" class="list" style="list-style-type:decimal">
<li>
<p id="P51">In collaboration with clinical personnel, collect relevant donor tissues and place in 50 ml conical tubes, submerging the tissues (e.g., whole tonsils, hysterectomies, or cervical biopsies) in transport media.
</p>
<p id="P52">More starter material, with greater epithelial surface area, will yield more keratinocytes and a greater chance of success. Ideally start with at least 10 mm × 10 mm of tissue. We have successfully used this protocol with smaller input (e.g., small cervical biopsies: &lt; 5 mm of tissue).</p>
</li>
<li><div class="p" id="P53">Store samples at 4°C overnight (~16 hrs).
<ol id="L8" class="list" style="list-style-type:lower-alpha">
<li><div class="p" id="P54">Keep tissues from multiple donors in separate tubes.</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P55">Tissues should be processed next day, and not stored for more than 2 days.</div></li>
</ol>
</div></li>
<li>
<p id="P56">Rinse tissue once in 1X D-PBS.
</p>
<p id="P57">Perform this and all subsequent steps at room temperature (unless otherwise stated for incubations) and in a biosafety cabinet, adhering to aseptic technique.</p>
</li>
<li><p id="P58">Observe gross morphology, measure tissue dimensions, and photograph for records.</p></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P59">(Optional) Dissect and reserve parts of the tissue (~5 mm in all dimension, containing epithelium) for histology or downstream molecular analysis
<ol id="L10" class="list" style="list-style-type:lower-alpha">
<li>
<div class="p" id="P60">Fix tissue in 10% buffered formalin for a minimum of 24 hours in a 1.5 ml microcentrifuge tube (with enough volume to cover the piece, 500 to 1000 μl should be sufficient for pieces ~5 mm in all dimensions), then wash twice using equal volumes of 70% EtOH. Samples can be stored in 70% EtOH at room temperature for several weeks if needed. Following embedding in paraffin and sectioning, these samples can be processed as described in <a href="#S54" class="usa-link">basic protocol 3</a>.
</div>
<div class="p" id="P61">Larger tissues (&gt;10 mm) should be incubated longer, to allow full penetration of fixative into tissue.</div>
</li>
<li><div class="p" id="P62">Flash-freeze tissues for molecular analysis in liquid nitrogen and store at −80°C.</div></li>
</ol>
</div></li>
<li>
<p id="P63">In a 10 cm dish, use forceps and scalpel with blade to remove the underlying hypodermis and loose connective tissue as much as possible while leaving the epithelial lining/casing intact (see <a href="#F2" class="usa-link">Fig. 2</a>).
</p>
<p id="P64">It is critical that the epithelial portion of the tissue is not discarded, as this contains the keratinocytes. The goal of this step is to remove as much of the non-epithelial tissue as possible so that a pure culture can be achieved.</p>
</li>
<li><p id="P65">Dissect the tissue into smaller pieces (&lt; 10 mm in size).</p></li>
<li><p id="P66">Place the tissue piece(s) in the wells of a 6-well plate, ensuring they are not overly crowded and can lay flat (and that they separate donor tissues are kept apart), and cover using 2 ml room temperature dispase II (2.4 U/ml in HBSS, with antibiotics and antimycotic added: penicillin and streptomycin at 1X, and amphotericin B at 0.625 μg/ml).</p></li>
<li><p id="P67">Incubate tissue overnight at 4°C (~16 hours).</p></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P68">Process tissue to isolate and create a suspension of keratinocytes:
<ol id="L12" class="list" style="list-style-type:lower-alpha">
<li><div class="p" id="P69">Transfer the tissues to a 10 cm tissue culture dish.</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P70">The epidermis is separated with forceps from any underlying dermal tissue remaining. Scrape these cells from the underlying tissue if the layer doesn’t separate cleanly off, and place the epidermal layer in a 50 ml tube containing 2 ml of 0.25% trypsin/EDTA.</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P71">Incubate the tissue in the 0.25% trypsin/EDTA at 37°C for 10 to 20 min to dissociate the epidermal cells, mixing gently every few minutes by swirling.</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P72">Inactivate the trypsin by adding 10 ml inactivation media, pipetting up and down 10 times to mix thoroughly.</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P73">Pass this solution (~12 ml) through a cell strainer filter (70 μm), into a 50 ml tube, rinse the 15 ml tube with 5 ml inactivation media, then centrifuge at 200 × <em>g</em> for 5 min. The cells can be counted and viability assessed via Trypan-blue exclusion at this stage.</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P74">Resuspend the pellet in complete F-media (including antibiotics and amphotericin B) and plate them onto irradiated J2 fibroblasts in a 10 cm tissue culture dish (as described in <a href="#S8" class="usa-link">Support Protocol 2</a>).</div></li>
</ol>
</div></li>
</ol>
<figure class="fig xbox font-sm" id="F2"><h4 class="obj_head">Figure 2.</h4>
<p class="img-box line-height-none margin-x-neg-2 tablet:margin-x-0 text-center"><img class="graphic" src="https://cdn.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/blobs/3a7a/11088941/a3070da882a2/nihms-1991549-f0002.jpg" loading="lazy" height="1268" width="1920" alt="Figure 2"></p>
<div class="p text-right font-secondary"><a href="figure/F2/" class="usa-link" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Open in a new tab</a></div>
<figcaption><p id="P786">Gross photograph of a palatine tonsil removed via tonsillectomy and ready to process (in a 10 cm dish, with a cm ruler underneath) for isolating primary keratinocytes. Arrows depict the epithelial casing (it is critical that this portion be kept, as it contains the keratinocytes) and the underlying hypodermis (and lymphoid) tissue.</p></figcaption></figure></section></section><section id="S8"><h2 class="pmc_sec_title">
<em>SUPPORT PROTOCOL 2:</em> Growth and maintenance of primary human epithelial cells in monolayer culture</h2>
<p id="P75">Primary human keratinocytes are used to seed 3D raft cultures described in <a href="#S22" class="usa-link">Basic Protocol 1</a>. Our lab cultures these cells in co-culture with terminally differentiated J2 fibroblast feeder cells as described by Rheinwald and Green (<a href="#R57" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R57">Rheinwald &amp; Green, 1975b</a>). This protocol describes how to culture and expand these primary cells.</p>
<section id="S9"><h3 class="pmc_sec_title">Materials</h3>
<section id="S10"><h4 class="pmc_sec_title">Reagents, solutions, and cell lines</h4>
<ul id="L14" class="list" style="list-style-type:none">
<li><p id="P76">Primary epithelial cells in culture: sub-confluent 10 cm plate</p></li>
<li><p id="P77">Versene (0.48 mM EDTA in PBS, ThermoFisher Scientific, cat. no. 15040066)</p></li>
<li><p id="P78">Dulbecco’s phosphate-buffered saline (D-PBS; ThermoFisher Scientific, cat. no. 14190–144)</p></li>
<li><p id="P79">0.25% trypsin/EDTA (ThermoFisher Scientific, cat. no. 25200056)</p></li>
<li><p id="P80">Rheinwald-Green media (F-media; see recipe)</p></li>
<li><p id="P81">J2 fibroblast growth media (see recipe)</p></li>
<li><p id="P82">0.4% Trypan blue (VWR, cat. no. 97063–702)</p></li>
<li><p id="P83">ROCK inhibitor (Y-27632; Chemdea, cat. no. CD0141)</p></li>
</ul></section><section id="S11"><h4 class="pmc_sec_title">Hardware and instruments</h4>
<ul id="L16" class="list" style="list-style-type:none">
<li><p id="P84">Humidified 5% CO<sub>2</sub> incubator</p></li>
<li><p id="P85">Humidified 10% CO<sub>2</sub> incubator</p></li>
<li><p id="P86">Inverted light microscope</p></li>
<li><p id="P87">Biosafety cabinet with vacuum aspiration system</p></li>
<li><p id="P88">Pasteur pipettes</p></li>
<li><p id="P89">Serological pipettes</p></li>
<li><p id="P90">15 ml conical tubes</p></li>
<li><p id="P91">Automated cell counter and counting slides</p></li>
<li><p id="P92">Centrifuge</p></li>
</ul></section></section><section id="S12"><h3 class="pmc_sec_title">Protocol steps</h3>
<ol id="L18" class="list" style="list-style-type:decimal">
<li>
<p id="P93">Culture J2 fibroblasts in J2 medium using standard sub-culturing techniques (see Current Protocols article: <a href="#R66" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R66">Takashima, 2001</a>).</p>
<p id="P94">Critical. Cells should be used at low passage. J2 cell morphology should be monitored to avoid transformation of the feeder culture.</p>
</li>
<li><p id="P95">Plate 1 × 10<sup>6</sup> feeders on a 10-cm dish and allow them to attach and spread overnight in a 37°C CO<sub>2</sub> incubator.</p></li>
<li><p id="P96">Irradiate cells with a dose of 6000R.</p></li>
<li>
<p id="P97">Change the medium to complete F-media and plate 200,000 primary cells (e.g., from Support Protocol 1, Step 10) onto the irradiated feeder monolayer.
</p>
<p id="P98">ROCK inhibitor (Y-27632) can be added to these cultures at a final concentration of 10 μM to conditionally immortalize these primary epithelial cells (<a href="#R10" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R10">Chapman et al., 2010</a>, <a href="#R11" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R11">2014</a>). It is critical that Y-27632 is removed before differentiating the cells using raft or RWV technologies.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p id="P99">Replace the media every 48 hours until cells reach 85–90% confluency.
</p>
<p id="P100">Critical. Cells should grow in individual colonies and should not contact neighboring colonies.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p id="P101">Remove 10 cm plate of primary epithelial cells (e.g., human tonsillar keratinocytes, HTKs; or human cervical keratinocytes, HCKs) from the incubator and confirm by microscope that they are ready to harvest: sub-confluent, just before colonies start to touch.</p>
<p id="P102">If this is the first passage of the isolated cells it is important that you preserve their viability and make sufficient cryovial stocks. The majority of the cells harvested should be used for making these stocks, continued culturing, or for experiments or other molecular extractions. Only a small number of cells (&lt; 10<sup>6</sup>) will be needed for DNA isolation.</p>
</li>
<li><p id="P103">In a biosafety cabinet, use a Pasteur pipette to vacuum aspirate the media from the cells, using the edge of the plate to avoid scraping the surface layer of cells.</p></li>
<li>
<p id="P104">Add 5 ml of Versene to the plate using a serological pipette, ensure full coverage by rocking back and forth and side-to-side, and incubate at room temperature for 1 min, then pipette the Versene up and down over the cells to help remove the feeder cells. Confirm by microscope that the feeders lift from the plate. It may be necessary to slightly agitate the plate by rocking back and forth, taking care not to spill the contents.</p>
<p id="P105">Versene will cause the J2 fibroblast feeder cells to detach whilst leaving the keratinocytes adhered.</p>
</li>
<li><p id="P106">Vacuum aspirate the Versene and suspended J2 feeder cells.</p></li>
<li><p id="P107">Rinse the cells in 5 ml D-PBS to help remove any residual J2 feeder cells.</p></li>
<li><p id="P108">Vacuum aspirate the D-PBS and any residual feeder cells.</p></li>
<li><p id="P109">Add 3 ml of 37°C 0.25% trypsin/EDTA, ensure full coverage of the surface of the plate by rocking back and forth and side-to-side, and incubate at 37°C until keratinocyte colonies are dissociated and detached from the plate (~5 to 10 min). Check by microscope often to ensure cells do not remain in trypsin longer than necessary.</p></li>
<li><p id="P110">Add 7 ml of F-media to inactivate the trypsin, pipette up/down, rinsing the plate, to create a cell suspension, and transfer this 10 ml total volume to a 50 ml conical tube. These cells can be counted, to determine the number of cells per ml, and used in downstream protocols (for seeding the basal keratinocyte layer in <a href="#S22" class="usa-link">Basic Protocol 1</a>; for PCR-based HPV screening in <a href="#S13" class="usa-link">Support Protocol 3</a>; and as a 2D monolayer control for RNA extraction in <a href="#S76" class="usa-link">Support Protocol 7</a> and RT-qPCR in <a href="#S81" class="usa-link">Basic Protocol 7</a>).</p></li>
</ol></section></section><section id="S13"><h2 class="pmc_sec_title">
<em>SUPPORT PROTOCOL 3:</em> PCR-based HPV screening of primary cell cultures</h2>
<p id="P111">HPV infections are prevalent. As such, it is possible that the primary human oral or cervical epithelial cells were infected at the time of isolation. This protocol uses a well-characterized degenerate primer PCR to amplify a 450 bp fragment of the L1 gene (<a href="#R44" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R44">Manos et al., 1989</a>; <a href="#R65" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R65">Tachezy et al., 1994</a>). This PCR can detect a wide array of HPV types. Since we typically experimentally infect these primary cells with HPV virions, we only use cell lines that are negative for HPV sequences.</p>
<section id="S14"><h3 class="pmc_sec_title">Materials</h3>
<section id="S15"><h4 class="pmc_sec_title">Reagents, solutions, and cell lines</h4>
<ul id="L20" class="list" style="list-style-type:none">
<li><p id="P112">Primary epithelial cells in culture: sub-confluent 10 cm plate (see Support Protocol 2)</p></li>
<li><p id="P113">Versene (0.48 mM EDTA in PBS, ThermoFisher Scientific, cat. no. 15040066)</p></li>
<li><p id="P114">Dulbecco’s phosphate-buffered saline (D-PBS; ThermoFisher Scientific, cat. no. 14190–144)</p></li>
<li><p id="P115">0.25% trypsin/EDTA (ThermoFisher Scientific, cat. no. 25200056)</p></li>
<li><p id="P116">Incomplete F-media (see recipe)</p></li>
<li><p id="P117">0.4% Trypan blue (VWR, cat. no. 97063–702)</p></li>
<li><p id="P118">DNeasy Blood &amp; Tissue Kit (Qiagen, cat. no. 69506)</p></li>
<li><p id="P119">ThermoFisher PCR kit (ThermoFisher Scientific, cat. no. EP0402)</p></li>
<li><p id="P120">dNTP mix, 2 mM each (made from dNTP set, ThermoFisher Scientific, cat. no. 10297018)</p></li>
<li><p id="P121">Nuclease-free water</p></li>
<li><p id="P122">MY09 primer 5’-CGTCCMARRGGAWACTGATC-3’ (<a href="#R44" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R44">Manos et al., 1989</a>)</p></li>
<li>
<p id="P123">MY11 primer 5’-GCMCAGGGWCATAAYAATGG-3’ (<a href="#R44" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R44">Manos et al., 1989</a>)</p>
<p id="P124">According to IUPAC DNA code: M = A or C; R = A or G; W = A or T; Y = C or T</p>
</li>
<li><p id="P125">GAPDH forward primer 5’-GGCAGCAGCAAGCATTCCT-3’ (<a href="#R69" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R69">Van Doorslaer et al., 2016</a>)</p></li>
<li><p id="P126">GAPDH reverse primer 5’-GCCCAACACCCCCAGTCA-3’ (<a href="#R69" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R69">Van Doorslaer et al., 2016</a>)</p></li>
<li><p id="P127">Positive control DNA (e.g., HPV18 plasmid, containing L1)</p></li>
<li><p id="P128">Negative control DNA (e.g., J2/3T3 feeder fibroblasts)</p></li>
<li><p id="P129">Agarose (Lonza, cat. no. 50074)</p></li>
<li><p id="P130">1x TAE buffer (see recipes)</p></li>
<li><p id="P131">Gel loading dye, Purple, 6X (New England Biolabs, cat. no. B7024S)</p></li>
<li><p id="P132">GeneRuler 1 kb Plus DNA Ladder (ThermoFisher Scientific, cat. no. SM1333)</p></li>
<li><p id="P133">Ethidium bromide (Fisher Scientific, cat. no. MP1ETBC1001)</p></li>
</ul></section><section id="S16"><h4 class="pmc_sec_title">Hardware and instruments</h4>
<ul id="L22" class="list" style="list-style-type:none">
<li><p id="P134">Humidified 5% CO<sub>2</sub> incubator</p></li>
<li><p id="P135">Humidified 10% CO<sub>2</sub> incubator</p></li>
<li><p id="P136">Inverted light microscope</p></li>
<li><p id="P137">Biosafety cabinet with vacuum aspiration system</p></li>
<li><p id="P138">Pasteur pipettes</p></li>
<li><p id="P139">Serological pipettes</p></li>
<li><p id="P140">50 ml conical tubes</p></li>
<li><p id="P141">Automated cell counter and counting slides</p></li>
<li><p id="P142">Centrifuge</p></li>
<li><p id="P143">Thermomixer or heat block, 56°C</p></li>
<li><p id="P144">Nanodrop spectrophotometer</p></li>
<li><p id="P145">200 μl PCR tubes</p></li>
<li><p id="P146">Thermocycler</p></li>
<li><p id="P147">100 ml graduated cylinder</p></li>
<li><p id="P148">500 ml Erlenmeyer flask</p></li>
<li><p id="P149">Microwave</p></li>
<li><p id="P150">Thermal protection gloves</p></li>
<li><p id="P151">Electrophoresis apparatus (casting tray, tape, comb, powerpack, electrodes)</p></li>
<li><p id="P152">Gel loading pipet tips</p></li>
<li><p id="P153">Staining tray</p></li>
<li><p id="P154">Rocking platform</p></li>
<li><p id="P155">Gel imaging dock (UV transilluminator, hood, and camera)</p></li>
</ul></section></section><section id="S17"><h3 class="pmc_sec_title">Protocol steps</h3>
<section id="S18"><h4 class="pmc_sec_title">Part 1 Total DNA extraction</h4>
<ol id="L24" class="list" style="list-style-type:decimal">
<li><p id="P156">Remove J2 feeders and collect primary cells as described in <a href="#S8" class="usa-link">Support Protocol 2</a>.</p></li>
<li>
<p id="P157">Calculate the required volume of cell suspension needed for DNA isolation.
</p>
<p id="P158">We find that starting with 7.5 × 10<sup>5</sup> cells for DNA isolation will typically yield ~10 to 20 μg of purified DNA: 50 to 100 ng/μl of 200 μl eluate.</p>
</li>
<li><p id="P159">Centrifuge cells 150 × <em>g</em> for 7 min.</p></li>
<li><p id="P160">Aspirate the supernatant carefully, without disturbing the pellet, then resuspend in 5 ml D-PBS to wash.</p></li>
<li><p id="P161">Centrifuge 150 × <em>g</em> for 7 min.</p></li>
<li>
<p id="P162">Aspirate supernatant, then proceed with DNA isolation (cell lysis).
</p>
<p id="P163">If you wish to perform DNA isolation at a future time you can flash freeze this pellet of cells in liquid nitrogen and store at −80°C. The cells will no longer be viable, but the DNA should remain stable, and we recommend flash-freezing and storing at such low temperatures in case you also need to preserve the samples for RNA isolation.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p id="P164">Extract DNA using the Qiagen DNeasy Blood &amp; Tissue Kit following instructions.
</p>
<p id="P165">We elute with 2 × 100 μl pre-warmed (56°C) molecular-grade nuclease-free water.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p id="P166">Measure DNA concentration and purity spectrophotometrically, using the same elution buffer as a blank.
</p>
<p id="P167">Concentration will depend on several factors, including the number of cells used for extraction, elution volume used, and the overall success of the cell lysis and DNA isolation procedure. Refer to your DNA isolation kit troubleshooting guide for tips on improving yield and purity.</p>
</li>
</ol></section><section id="S19"><h4 class="pmc_sec_title">Part 2 PCR detection of HPV L1 gene</h4>
<ol id="L26" class="list" style="list-style-type:decimal">
<li><div class="p" id="P168">Set up PCR reactions by making a master mix containing the following components:
<ol id="L28" class="list" style="list-style-type:lower-alpha">
<li><div class="p" id="P169">ddH<sub>2</sub>O to 25 μl total volume (taking into account template DNA)</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P170">2.5 μl 10X <em>Taq</em> buffer with KCl (1X final)</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P171">2.5 μl dNTP mix 2mM (0.2 mM final)</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P172">0.75 μl ea of HPV L1 MY09/11 degenerate primers 10 mM (0.3 mM final)</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P173">2 μl MgCl<sub>2</sub> 25 mM (2 mM final)</div></li>
<li>
<div class="p" id="P174">0.125 μl <em>Taq</em> polymerase 5 U/μl (0.025 U/μl final)
</div>
<div class="p" id="P175">Allow 10% extra to account for pipette errors.</div>
</li>
</ol>
</div></li>
<li><p id="P176">Aliquot master mix to 200 μl PCR tubes.</p></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P177">Add template
<ol id="L30" class="list" style="list-style-type:lower-alpha">
<li><div class="p" id="P178">No template control: nuclease-free water (enough to bring final volume to 25 μl)</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P179">100 ng template genomic DNA</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P180">1 ng of positive control plasmid DNA.</div></li>
</ol>
</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P181">Run PCR with the following thermocycler parameters:
<ol id="L32" class="list" style="list-style-type:lower-alpha">
<li><div class="p" id="P182">Initial denaturation 95°C for 5 min</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P183">35 cycles of
<ul id="L34" class="list" style="list-style-type:disc">
<li><div class="p" id="P184">Denature 95°C for 1 min</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P185">Anneal 55°C for 2 min</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P186">Extension 72°C for 2 min</div></li>
</ul>
</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P187">Final extension 72°C for 3 min</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P188">Hold at 4°C</div></li>
</ol>
</div></li>
<li><p id="P189">Store PCR products short-term at 4°C and long-term at −20°C.</p></li>
</ol></section><section id="S20"><h4 class="pmc_sec_title">Part 3 PCR detection of a human gene to confirm DNA extraction</h4>
<ol id="L36" class="list" style="list-style-type:decimal">
<li><div class="p" id="P190">Set up PCR reactions by making a master mix containing the following components:
<ol id="L38" class="list" style="list-style-type:lower-alpha">
<li><div class="p" id="P191">ddH<sub>2</sub>O to 25 μl total volume (taking into account template DNA)</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P192">2.5 μl 10X <em>Taq</em> buffer with KCl (1X final)</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P193">2.5 μl dNTP mix 2mM (0.2 mM final)</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P194">0.75 μl ea. of GAPDH primers 10 mM (0.3 mM final)</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P195">2 μl MgCl<sub>2</sub> 25 mM (2 mM final)</div></li>
<li>
<div class="p" id="P196">0.125 μl <em>Taq</em> polymerase 5 U/μl (0.025 U/μl final)
</div>
<div class="p" id="P197">Allow 10% extra to account for pipette.</div>
</li>
</ol>
</div></li>
<li><p id="P198">Aliquot master mix to 200 μl PCR tubes.</p></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P199">Add template
<ol id="L40" class="list" style="list-style-type:lower-alpha">
<li><div class="p" id="P200">No template control: nuclease-free water (enough to bring final volume to 25 μl)</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P201">100 ng template genomic DNA</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P202">1 ng of positive control plasmid DNA.</div></li>
</ol>
</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P203">Run PCR with the following thermocycler parameters:
<ol id="L42" class="list" style="list-style-type:lower-alpha">
<li><div class="p" id="P204">Initial denaturation 95°C for 5 min</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P205">35 cycles of
<ol id="L44" class="list" style="list-style-type:lower-roman">
<li><div class="p" id="P206">Denature 95°C for 1 min</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P207">Anneal 55°C for 2 min</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P208">Extension 72°C for 2 min</div></li>
</ol>
</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P209">Final extension 72°C for 3 min</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P210">Hold at 4°C</div></li>
</ol>
</div></li>
<li><p id="P211">Store PCR products short-term at 4°C and long-term at −20°C.</p></li>
</ol></section><section id="S21"><h4 class="pmc_sec_title">Part 4 Visualize specific PCR amplicons by gel electrophoresis</h4>
<ol id="L46" class="list" style="list-style-type:decimal">
<li><p id="P212">Cast a gel by mixing agarose powder (2 g for a 2% gel) with 100 ml 1x TAE.</p></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P213">Once fully solidified, cover the gel with 1x TAE, and remove the comb.
<ol id="L48" class="list" style="list-style-type:lower-alpha"><li><div class="p" id="P214">Ensure wells are intact.</div></li></ol>
</div></li>
<li>
<p id="P215">Load samples with gel loading pipet tips after mixing 10 μl of PCR product with 2 μl 6x loading dye. Include 5 μl of GeneRuler 1 kb Plus DNA ladder.
</p>
<p id="P216">We recommend leaving empty wells between each sample or ladder-containing lane in case there is any accidental spillover from one well into the other, which could confound interpretation between adjacent samples.</p>
</li>
<li><p id="P217">Run the gel until the dye front is 2/3 down the gel.</p></li>
<li><p id="P218">Stain gel using Ethidium Bromide or other DNA stain.</p></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P219">Image the DNA gel.
<ol id="L50" class="list" style="list-style-type:lower-alpha">
<li><div class="p" id="P220">An HPV specific amplicon is expected around 450 basepairs.</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P221">A GAPDH specific amplicon is expected around 137 basepairs.</div></li>
</ol>
</div></li>
</ol></section></section></section><section id="S22"><h2 class="pmc_sec_title">
<em>BASIC PROTOCOL 1:</em> Establishing human primary cell derived 3D organotypic raft cultures</h2>
<p id="P222">This protocol highlights the steps taken to generate a full-thickness 3D organotypic raft tissue. First, we establish a dermal equivalent containing collagen and fibroblasts. A basal layer of keratinocytes (HPV-positive or negative) is seeded onto this dermal equivalent. Finally, we will lift these rafts to the air-liquid interface and allow the tissue to differentiate for several weeks. We will show examples of human foreskin, human cervical, and human tonsillar epithelia. The cervical cells were infected with HPV18 before starting the differentiation process. We will demonstrate that, despite using the same method, the organotypic tissues display features reminiscent of the original tissue.</p>
<section id="S23"><h3 class="pmc_sec_title">Materials</h3>
<section id="S24"><h4 class="pmc_sec_title">Reagents, solutions, and cell lines</h4>
<ul id="L52" class="list" style="list-style-type:none">
<li>
<p id="P223">Human fibroblasts hTERT immortalized (e.g., HFF-hTERT RRID:CVCL_VC40).
</p>
<p id="P224">Alternatively, can use mouse J2/3T3 or primary human fibroblasts, either foreskin-derived or from origin site being modeled</p>
</li>
<li><p id="P225">Primary human epithelial cells isolated in <a href="#S3" class="usa-link">Support Protocol 1</a></p></li>
<li><p id="P226">Fibroblast growth media (see recipe)</p></li>
<li><p id="P227">10x Hanks’ Balanced Salt Solution with phenol red (Sigma, cat. no. H4385–100ML)</p></li>
<li><p id="P228">4 M NaOH</p></li>
<li><p id="P229">Fetal Bovine Serum (FBS)</p></li>
<li><p id="P230">Rat Tail Collagen, Type I (Corning, cat. no. 354236): 4 mg/ml</p></li>
<li><p id="P231">Dulbecco’s phosphate-buffered saline (D-PBS; ThermoFisher Scientific, cat. no. 14190–144)</p></li>
<li><p id="P232">0.25% Trypsin/EDTA (ThermoFisher Scientific, cat. no. 25200056)</p></li>
<li><p id="P233">0.4% Trypan blue (VWR, cat. no. 97063–702)</p></li>
<li><p id="P234">Differentiation Media (see recipe)</p></li>
<li><p id="P235">Complete F-media (see recipe)</p></li>
<li><p id="P236">10% buffered formalin (Fisher Scientific, cat. no. SF98–4)</p></li>
<li><p id="P237">70% ethanol</p></li>
<li><p id="P238">Liquid nitrogen</p></li>
</ul></section><section id="S25"><h4 class="pmc_sec_title">Hardware and instruments</h4>
<ul id="L54" class="list" style="list-style-type:none">
<li><p id="P239">Vacuum aspirator</p></li>
<li><p id="P240">Pasteur pipettes</p></li>
<li><p id="P241">Pipettes</p></li>
<li><p id="P242">Microscope</p></li>
<li><p id="P243">50 ml conical tubes</p></li>
<li><p id="P244">1.5 ml microcentrifuge tubes</p></li>
<li><p id="P245">Automated cell counter and counting slides</p></li>
<li><p id="P246">Centrifuge and rotor for 50 ml conical tubes</p></li>
<li><p id="P247">48-well plates</p></li>
<li><p id="P248">Small container (large enough to hold 50 ml conical tube and ice)</p></li>
<li><p id="P249">CO<sub>2</sub> incubator</p></li>
<li><p id="P250">6-well plates</p></li>
<li><p id="P251">Membrane inserts (Millipore, cat. no. PICM0RG50)</p></li>
<li><p id="P252">Sterile forceps</p></li>
<li><p id="P253">Sterile microspatulas (such as Fisher Scientific, cat. no. 21-401-10)</p></li>
<li><p id="P254">Parafilm</p></li>
<li><p id="P255">−80°C freezer</p></li>
</ul></section></section><section id="S26"><h3 class="pmc_sec_title">Protocol steps</h3>
<p id="P256">This protocol will generate 12 medium-sized (<a href="#R33" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R33">Jackson et al., 2019</a>) 3D organotypic raft tissues, which contract over time from their initial diameter of ~10 mm to ~5 mm</p>
<section id="S27"><h4 class="pmc_sec_title">Day #1 – Prepare dermal equivalents</h4>
<ul id="L56" class="list" style="list-style-type:none">
<li>
<span class="label">1</span><div class="display-inline p" id="P257">Propagate and harvest human foreskin fibroblasts (HFF-tert) cells
<ol id="L58" class="list" style="list-style-type:lower-alpha">
<li><div class="p" id="P258">Viability should exceed 90% by Trypan blue exclusion</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P259">Protocol requires 80,000 cells per raft (A total of 960,000 fibroblasts for this protocol)</div></li>
</ol>
</div>
</li>
<li>
<span class="label">2</span><p class="display-inline" id="P260">Pellet the cells by centrifugation (7 min, 150 × <em>g</em>)</p>
</li>
<li>
<span class="label">3</span><p class="display-inline" id="P261">Resuspend in 960 μl cold FBS (1 × 10<sup>6</sup> cells/ml)</p>
</li>
<li>
<span class="label">4</span><div class="display-inline p" id="P262">Prepare dermal mixture by combining:
<ol id="L60" class="list" style="list-style-type:lower-alpha">
<li><div class="p" id="P263">3.75 ml collagen</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P264">0.5 ml Hanks medium</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P265">dropwise add 22.5 μl of 4M NaOH (We recommend adding this in 2.5 μl increments)</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P266">960 μl fibroblast/FBS, mix carefully with pipette and swirling tube by hand</div></li>
</ol>
</div>
<p id="P267">It is critical that this is performed in a pre-cooled (−20°C freezer) 50 ml conical tube that is stored on ice.
</p>
<p id="P268">Ensure that the collagen is neutralized prior to adding the fibroblast cells
</p>
<p id="P269">Do not introduce air bubbles</p>
</li>
<li>
<span class="label">5</span><div class="display-inline p" id="P270">Seed 400 μl of dermal mixture per well into 12 wells of a pre-labelled 48 well plate.
<ol id="L62" class="list" style="list-style-type:lower-alpha"><li><div class="p" id="P271">Check under microscope to confirm all dermal equivalents have homogenous fibroblasts</div></li></ol>
</div>
</li>
<li>
<span class="label">6</span><p class="display-inline" id="P272">Incubate in 37°C 5% CO<sub>2</sub> incubator for 20 min to solidify. Confirm that the dermal equivalents turn opaque.</p>
</li>
<li>
<span class="label">7</span><p class="display-inline" id="P273">Carefully add 400 μl fibroblast growth media to each raft, along the side of the well.</p>
</li>
<li>
<span class="label">8</span><p class="display-inline" id="P274">Incubate overnight (~16–18 hrs) at 37°C, 5% CO<sub>2</sub></p>
</li>
</ul></section><section id="S28"><h4 class="pmc_sec_title">Day #2 – Seed basal keratinocyte layer</h4>
<ul id="L64" class="list" style="list-style-type:none">
<li>
<span class="label">9</span><div class="display-inline p" id="P275">Check dermal equivalents from Day #1
<ol id="L66" class="list" style="list-style-type:lower-alpha">
<li><div class="p" id="P276">Confirm that the fibroblasts are homogeneously distributed throughout the dermis and that they appear viable and elongated.</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P277">Confirm the color of the dermal equivalents: should be a little more acidic, from pinkish red to peachy orange, and free of contaminants.</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P278">Confirm integrity of the dermal equivalents: should all be intact, adhered to the bottom of the well, with no obvious air bubbles</div></li>
</ol>
</div>
</li>
<li>
<span class="label">10</span><p class="display-inline" id="P279">Harvest the keratinocytes as per Support Protocol 2 (Steps 6 to 13). The protocol needs 250k cells for each medium-sized raft.</p>
</li>
<li>
<span class="label">11</span><p class="display-inline" id="P280">Remove liquid from atop the dermal equivalents with aspiration initially (taking care not to get too close to the layer) and a pipettor to remove any remaining liquid.</p>
</li>
<li>
<span class="label">12</span><p class="display-inline" id="P281">Resuspend keratinocytes to 250k/50 μl keratinocyte growth media.</p>
</li>
<li>
<span class="label">13</span><p class="display-inline" id="P282">Deposit mixed keratinocytes drop-wise on top of dermal equivalents, then rock back and forth side to side front to back, and angle in each direction to distribute. Check that keratinocytes are evenly distributed under the microscope. You should be able to focus through the dermal layer and see the basal keratinocytes seeded on top</p>
</li>
<li>
<span class="label">14</span><p class="display-inline" id="P283">Incubate cells 2 hr at 37°C 5% CO<sub>2</sub> to allow initial adherence of this basal keratinocyte layer</p>
</li>
<li>
<span class="label">15</span><div class="display-inline p" id="P284">Check under microscope for adherence
<ol id="L68" class="list" style="list-style-type:lower-alpha"><li><div class="p" id="P285">Should not observe too many floating cells if you move the plate gently to check.</div></li></ol>
</div>
</li>
<li>
<span class="label">16</span><p class="display-inline" id="P286"><strong>Carefully/slowly</strong> add 400 μl F-media, moving around the edge of the well in a circular motion, so that loosely adherence cells won’t be washed to one side. Check by microscope to ensure that no obvious detachment of cells has occurred.</p>
</li>
<li>
<span class="label">17</span><p class="display-inline" id="P287">Incubate overnight at 37°C 5% CO<sub>2</sub></p>
</li>
</ul></section><section id="S29"><h4 class="pmc_sec_title">Day #3 – Lifting to the air-liquid interface</h4>
<section id="S30"><h5 class="pmc_sec_title">Proceed with lifting ~24 hours post-seeding of the keratinocytes</h5>
<ul id="L70" class="list" style="list-style-type:none">
<li>
<span class="label">18</span><div class="display-inline p" id="P288">Observe the 48-well plate cultures by microscope. Ensure that the basal layer of the raft tissue appears attached and 100% confluent. Confirm the fibroblasts are still homogeneously distributed and viable, with elongated phenotype.
<ol id="L72" class="list" style="list-style-type:lower-alpha">
<li><div class="p" id="P289">Media should be peachy-yellow, given proliferation of the basal keratinocytes as they become 100% confluent on-top of the dermal equivalent (pink media indicates that cells were likely not viable, or incorrect pH at time of seeding; peachy-yellow (with turbidity) could also be a sign of contamination.</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P290">Submerged cultures should appear intact: cylindrical and fully adhered to the bottom of the wells.</div></li>
</ol>
</div>
</li>
<li>
<span class="label">19</span><p class="display-inline" id="P291">Pre-label 6-well plate as per experimental design.</p>
</li>
<li>
<span class="label">20</span><p class="display-inline" id="P292">Aliquot exactly 1.1 ml of 37°C differentiation media into the wells of the 6-well plate. Ensure that the media completely covers the bottom surface of each well.</p>
</li>
<li>
<span class="label">21</span><div class="display-inline p" id="P293">Using sterile forceps, place membrane inserts into the media-filled wells of the 6-well plate: lower into the well at a slight angle, so that the bottom surface of the membrane contacts the media at one end and fully wets the bottom of the membrane evenly as you lower it in.
<ol id="L74" class="list" style="list-style-type:lower-alpha"><li>
<div class="p" id="P294">Rotate the filter in the media-filled wells until the filters are fully wet.
</div>
<div class="p" id="P295">
<strong>Critical:</strong> These membranes are hydrophobic and are difficult to wet. If bubbles form underneath the membrane, lift them on an angle with forceps and use the side of a sterile pipette tip to displace any bubbles, taking care not to puncture the membrane, before placing them back in flat.</div>
</li></ol>
</div>
</li>
<li>
<span class="label">22</span><p class="display-inline" id="P296">In the 48-well plate, carefully remove F-media from the submerged cultures (dermal equivalent with basal layer of keratinocytes on top) by holding the plate on an angle and using a pipette (1000 μl, then 200 μl) to remove the liquid without disturbing the culture.</p>
</li>
<li>
<span class="label">23</span><p class="display-inline" id="P297">Loosen the rafts within the well by sliding a 200 μl pipette tip carefully around the outside edge.</p>
</li>
<li>
<span class="label">24</span><div class="display-inline p" id="P298">Use sterile rounded end scoops to transfer rafts from the 48-well plate to the top of the membrane inserts in the 6-well plate.
<ol id="L76" class="list" style="list-style-type:lower-alpha">
<li><div class="p" id="P299">Two medium-sized rafts can fit on a 6-well membrane insert. Ensure they are not touching each other or the plastic edge of the membrane.</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P300">Take care to ensure the keratinocyte side stays up, and you do not pinch or crush the rafts. This process takes careful fine-motor skills.</div></li>
</ol>
</div>
</li>
<li>
<span class="label">25</span><p class="display-inline" id="P301">Remove excess liquid that builds up around the rafts on top the membrane shortly after lifting.</p>
</li>
<li>
<span class="label">26</span><p class="display-inline" id="P302">Incubate rafts at 37°C 5% CO<sub>2</sub> for 20 min, then remove any additional excess liquid that builds up around the rafts, and ensure the rafts are well-positioned and not touching each other or overlapping the edge of the membrane. Gently move them if needed with a 200 μl pipette tip.</p>
</li>
<li>
<span class="label">27</span><p class="display-inline" id="P303">Incubate 37°C 5% CO<sub>2</sub> for the duration of the rafting experiment (1 to 3 weeks, typically 2 weeks), changing media every 48 hours.</p>
</li>
</ul></section></section></section><section id="S31"><h3 class="pmc_sec_title">Media changes</h3>
<ul id="L78" class="list" style="list-style-type:none">
<li>
<span class="label">28</span><p class="display-inline" id="P304">After 48 hours, aspirate media from 6-well plates using a pipette along the side of the well, being careful not to flip the membrane insert or disrupt the rafts.</p>
</li>
<li>
<span class="label">29</span><div class="display-inline p" id="P305">Add exactly 1.1 ml total of differentiation media to the side of the well, so it spreads underneath the membrane.
<ol id="L80" class="list" style="list-style-type:lower-alpha"><li><div class="p" id="P306">If bubbles form under the membrane, or the media doesn’t fully cover the bottom, use a sterile pipette tip to rotate the membrane insert so bubbles are pushed to the side and the membrane is fully contacting the media</div></li></ol>
</div>
</li>
<li>
<span class="label">30</span><p class="display-inline" id="P307">Once the rafts are ready to harvest, with 2 weeks typically sufficient for full epithelial stratification, they can be processed for downstream analyses.</p>
</li>
</ul></section><section id="S32"><h3 class="pmc_sec_title">Tissue collection for histology</h3>
<ul id="L82" class="list" style="list-style-type:none">
<li>
<span class="label">31</span><p class="display-inline" id="P308">Use a microspatula or forceps to carefully transfer the entire raft into 500 μl of 10% buffered formalin within a 1.5 ml microcentrifuge tube.</p>
</li>
<li>
<span class="label">32</span><p class="display-inline" id="P309">Incubate the raft tissue for 24 hours at room temperature to allow the fixative to permeate.</p>
</li>
<li>
<span class="label">33</span><p class="display-inline" id="P310">Remove the formalin and gently wash the raft twice with 500 μl 70% ethanol</p>
</li>
<li>
<span class="label">34</span><div class="display-inline p" id="P311">Store in 500 μl 70% ethanol at room temperature until ready for histological processing.
<ol id="L84" class="list" style="list-style-type:lower-alpha">
<li><div class="p" id="P312">Proceed with the histological processing as soon as possible, within a few weeks at maximum)</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P313">To minimize evaporation of the 70% ethanol, seal the 1.5 ml centrifuge tubes with parafilm</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P314">The rafts should be bisected and embedded in paraffin so that a clear cross-section of the strata is visible.</div></li>
</ol>
</div>
</li>
</ul></section><section id="S33"><h3 class="pmc_sec_title">Tissue collection for molecular processing</h3>
<ul id="L86" class="list" style="list-style-type:none"><li>
<span class="label">35</span><div class="display-inline p" id="P315">Separate the epidermal layer from the dermis (collagen and fibroblasts).
<ol id="L88" class="list" style="list-style-type:lower-alpha">
<li><div class="p" id="P316">Use two sets of sterile forceps (one to hold the raft in place, and the other to grab an edge of the epidermis) and peel off the epidermis of the dermis.</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P317">Transfer the epidermal compartment and the dermal compartment to separate 1.5 ml microcentrifuge tubes.</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P318">Flash-freeze the tissues by suspending in liquid nitrogen</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P319">Store frozen tissues at −80°C.</div></li>
</ol>
</div>
</li></ul>
<p id="P320">Photographs of the rafting process are shown in <a href="#F3" class="usa-link">Fig. 3</a>.</p>
<figure class="fig xbox font-sm" id="F3"><h4 class="obj_head">Figure 3.</h4>
<p class="img-box line-height-none margin-x-neg-2 tablet:margin-x-0 text-center"><img class="graphic" src="https://cdn.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/blobs/3a7a/11088941/f54ad5772087/nihms-1991549-f0003.jpg" loading="lazy" height="1109" width="1920" alt="Figure 3"></p>
<div class="p text-right font-secondary"><a href="figure/F3/" class="usa-link" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Open in a new tab</a></div>
<figcaption><p id="P787">3D organotypic raft culturing process. Rafts are prepared over an initial period of 3 days, Day 1 prepare the dermal equivalent (see photograph above of the solidified collagen-fibroblast mixture in a 48-well plate). On Day 2 the basal layer of keratinocytes is seeded atop the dermal equivalent containing active fibroblasts (note the pH color change from reddish pink to peachy orange). On Day 3 the cultures are lifted to the air-liquid interface (see photograph depicting rafts on their membranes within a 6-well plate). These lifted rafts are cultured for two weeks, changing media every 48 hrs (see photograph, depicting the rafts with visual opacity due to differentiation and stratification). Note that the rafts contract during growth (compare diameter of raft at time of lifting vs. at harvest)</p></figcaption></figure></section></section><section id="S34"><h2 class="pmc_sec_title">
<em>SUPPORT PROTOCOL 4:</em> Growth and maintenance of human A2EN cells as monolayer culture</h2>
<p id="P321">We use human, cervical A2EN cells to seed the rotating wall vessel bioreactors and generate the 3D cervical epithelial cell model. This protocol describes how to thaw, culture, and expand the A2EN cells.</p>
<section id="S35"><h3 class="pmc_sec_title">Materials</h3>
<section id="S36"><h4 class="pmc_sec_title">Reagents, solutions, and cell lines</h4>
<ul id="L90" class="list" style="list-style-type:none">
<li><p id="P322">Human endocervical EC line (A2EN)</p></li>
<li><p id="P323">Gibco Keratinocyte serum-free medium (1X), without calcium chloride (Thermo Scientific, cat. no. 37010022)</p></li>
<li><p id="P324">Invivogen Primocin, 50 mg/ml (Thermo Scientific, cat. no. NC9392943)</p></li>
<li><p id="P325">Calcium chloride dihydrate, certified ACS (Fisher Scientific, cat. no. C79–500)</p></li>
<li><p id="P326">Corning 0.5% trypsin, 0.1% EDTA in HBSS without calcium, magnesium and sodium bicarbonate (Fisher Scientific, cat. no. MT25053CI)</p></li>
<li><p id="P327">Corning RPMI 1640 medium, 1X with L-glutamine (Fisher Scientific, cat. no. MT10040CV)</p></li>
<li><p id="P328">Corning regular fetal bovine serum (Fisher Scientific, cat. no. MT35010CV</p></li>
<li><p id="P329">Dubecco’s phosphate-buffered saline, 1X (Fisher Scientific, cat. no. MT21031CV)</p></li>
<li><p id="P330">Invitrogen 0.4% Trypan blue solution (Fisher Scientific, cat no. <a href="https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/nuccore/T10282" class="usa-link" data-ga-action="click_feat_suppl" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">T10282</a>)</p></li>
</ul></section><section id="S37"><h4 class="pmc_sec_title">Hardware and instruments</h4>
<ul id="L92" class="list" style="list-style-type:none">
<li><p id="P331">Falcon T25 25 cm<sup>2</sup> tissue culture treated flask (Fisher Scientific, cat. no. 10-126-10)</p></li>
<li><p id="P332">Falcon T75 75 cm<sup>2</sup> tissue culture treated flask (Fisher Scientific, cat. no. 10-126-11)</p></li>
<li><p id="P333">Falcon T150 150 cm<sup>2</sup> tissue culture treated flask (Fisher Scientific, cat. no. 08-772-48)</p></li>
<li><p id="P334">15 ml conical tubes</p></li>
<li><p id="P335">50 ml conical tubes</p></li>
<li><p id="P336">Autoclave sterilizer</p></li>
<li><p id="P337">Inverted light microscope</p></li>
<li><p id="P338">0.5 ml microcentrifuge tubes</p></li>
<li><p id="P339">1.5 ml microcentrifuge tubes</p></li>
</ul></section></section><section id="S38"><h3 class="pmc_sec_title">Protocol steps</h3>
<ol id="L94" class="list" style="list-style-type:decimal">
<li><p id="P340">Rapidly thaw a 1 ml frozen aliquot of human A2EN cells (~1×10<sup>6</sup> cells/ml) in a 37°C water bath.</p></li>
<li><p id="P341">Slowly add cells in a drop-wise manner to 9 ml pre-warmed (37°C) complete KFSM in a 15 ml conical tube.</p></li>
<li><p id="P342">Centrifuge cells at 322 × <em>g</em> for 5 minutes at room temperature. Remove and discard supernatant. Resuspend cells in 5 ml pre-warmed complete KFSM medium.</p></li>
<li><p id="P343">Transfer cells to a T25 25 cm<sup>2</sup> flask. Incubate at 37°C, 5% CO<sub>2</sub>. Monitor daily by light microscopy and change medium every 2–3 days until cells reach 90–95% confluency.</p></li>
<li><p id="P344">Remove and discard spent culture medium. Detach monolayer A2EN cells by treatment with 0.5 ml 0.5% trypsin-EDTA solution at 37°C, 5% CO<sub>2</sub> for 5–10 minutes. Suspend A2EN cells in 9.5 ml neutralization medium and transfer to a sterile 15 ml conical tube. Harvest cells by centrifugation (see <strong>step 3)</strong>. Discard supernatant and resuspend A2EN cells in 10 ml pre-warmed complete KFSM medium.</p></li>
<li><p id="P345">Subculture A2EN cells into a T75 cm<sup>2</sup> flask and add 5 ml complete KFSM medium to a final volume of 15 ml. Incubate cells at 37°C, 5% CO<sub>2</sub>. Subculture A2EN monolayer cells every 2–3 days by repeating <strong>step 6</strong>.</p></li>
<li><p id="P346">When A2EN monolayer cells reach 90–95% confluency, detach, harvest, and resuspend A2EN cells according to <strong>step 6.</strong> Transfer A2EN cells into a T150 cm<sup>2</sup> flask and adjust to 25 ml with pre-warmed complete KFSM medium. Continue incubating at 37°C, 5% CO<sub>2</sub> until A2EN monolayer cells reach 90–95% confluency.</p></li>
</ol></section></section><section id="S39"><h2 class="pmc_sec_title">
<em>SUPPORT PROTOCOL 5:</em> Preparing the slow turning lateral vessel bioreactor</h2>
<p id="P347">This protocol describes the steps taken to prepare the slow-turning lateral vessel (STLV) bioreactor system prior to culturing human A2EN cervical epithelial cells.</p>
<section id="S40"><h3 class="pmc_sec_title">Materials</h3>
<section id="S41"><h4 class="pmc_sec_title">Reagents, solutions, and cell lines</h4>
<ul id="L96" class="list" style="list-style-type:none">
<li><p id="P348">70% Ethanol</p></li>
<li><p id="P349">Sterile dH<sub>2</sub>O</p></li>
</ul></section><section id="S42"><h4 class="pmc_sec_title">Hardware and instruments</h4>
<ul id="L98" class="list" style="list-style-type:none">
<li><p id="P350">Slow-turning lateral vessel (STLV) bioreactor system (55 ml autoclavable STLV bioreactor, rotator base and speed control power supply) (SYNTHECON)</p></li>
<li><p id="P351">55 ml disposable high-aspect rotating wall vessel (HARV) (SYNTHECON)</p></li>
<li><p id="P352">Smith’s Medical ASD sterile one-way stop cocks (Fisher Scientific, cat. no. NC9889364)</p></li>
<li><p id="P353">Sterile 5 ml Luer-lock syringes (Fisher Scientific, cat. no. 14-955-458)</p></li>
<li><p id="P354">Sterile 10 ml Luer-lock syringes (Fisher Scientific, cat. no. 14-955-459)</p></li>
<li><p id="P355">Sterilization pouch</p></li>
<li><p id="P356">Autoclave sterilizer</p></li>
</ul></section></section><section id="S43"><h3 class="pmc_sec_title">Protocol steps</h3>
<ol id="L100" class="list" style="list-style-type:decimal">
<li><p id="P357">Assemble the STLV bioreactor according to the manufacturer’s instructions.</p></li>
<li><p id="P358">Decontaminate the STLV bioreactor by filling with 70% (v/v) ethanol through the central port. Seal the central port with the provided plug and incubate overnight at room temperature. Remove ethanol and repeat overnight incubation in 70% ethanol.</p></li>
<li><p id="P359">Remove ethanol and fill STLV bioreactor with sterile ddH<sub>2</sub>O. Incubate overnight at room temperature. Remove ddH<sub>2</sub>O and repeat overnight incubation in fresh sterile ddH<sub>2</sub>O. Remove ddH<sub>2</sub>O. Remove the central port and wrap in aluminum foil. Loosen STLV bioreactor unit screws using the tool provided by the vendor. Place wrapped central port and STLV bioreactor unit in a sterilization pouch.</p></li>
<li><p id="P360">Autoclave at 110°C for 20 minutes and allow the unit to cool. Tighten screws and attach the sterile one-way stop cocks to each side port.</p></li>
</ol></section></section><section id="S44"><h2 class="pmc_sec_title">
<em>SUPPORT PROTOCOL 6:</em> Preparing the cytodex-3 microcarrier beads</h2>
<p id="P361">During suspension growth inside the slow-turning lateral vessel bioreactor, the epithelial cells will attach to and grow on Cytodex-3 collagen-coated microcarrier beads allowing the cells to grow under physiologically relevant low fluid‐shear conditions.</p>
<p id="P362">This protocol describes the steps taken to prepare the Cytodex-3 microcarrier beads before culturing cells within the RWV bioreactor.</p>
<section id="S45"><h3 class="pmc_sec_title">Materials</h3>
<section id="S46"><h4 class="pmc_sec_title">Reagents, solutions, and cell lines</h4>
<ul id="L102" class="list" style="list-style-type:none">
<li><p id="P363">Sterile Dulbecco’s phosphate-buffered solution, 1X (Fisher Scientific, cat. no. MT21031CV)</p></li>
<li><p id="P364">Neutralization medium (see recipe)</p></li>
<li><p id="P365">Gibco Keratinocyte serum-free medium (1X), without calcium chloride (Thermo Scientific, cat. no. 37010022)</p></li>
</ul></section><section id="S47"><h4 class="pmc_sec_title">Hardware and instruments</h4>
<ul id="L104" class="list" style="list-style-type:none">
<li><p id="P366">Cytodex-3 collagen-coated microcarrier beads (Sigma Aldrich, cat. no. C3275–10G)</p></li>
<li><p id="P367">Autoclave sterilizer</p></li>
</ul></section></section><section id="S48"><h3 class="pmc_sec_title">Protocol steps</h3>
<ol id="L106" class="list" style="list-style-type:decimal">
<li><p id="P368">Add 300 mg of Cytodex-3 microcarrier beads to a 50 ml conical tube containing 25 ml D-PBS.</p></li>
<li><p id="P369">Incubate overnight at room temperature to allow beads to hydrate.</p></li>
<li>
<p id="P370">Autoclave beads at 110°C for 20 min. Allow beads to cool to room temperature.
</p>
<div class="p" id="P371">Ensure the tube remains in upright position during hydration and autoclaving to prevent microcarrier beads from adhering to the tube walls above the liquid-air interface. Wall-adherent microcarrier beads will decrease the ability of cells to form 3D cellular aggregates.
<ol id="L108" class="list" style="list-style-type:lower-alpha"><li><div class="p" id="P372">Hydrated and autoclaved Cytodex-3 microcarrier beads in D-PBS may be stored up to one week at room temperature.</div></li></ol>
</div>
</li>
<li><p id="P373">Allow beads to settle to the bottom of the tube and remove the upper layer of D-PBS. Wash beads with 25 ml neutralization medium. Allow beads to settle and remove and discard the neutralization medium.</p></li>
<li><p id="P374">Repeat wash procedure with 25 ml neutralization medium and allow beads to settle. Remove and discard the neutralization medium.</p></li>
<li><p id="P375">Wash beads with 25 ml complete KFSM medium. Allow beads to settle and repeat wash with 10 ml complete KFSM medium. Use immediately for seeding and differentiating 3D human cervical cells in the rotating wall vessel bioreactor (see Basic Protocol 2)</p></li>
</ol></section></section><section id="S49"><h2 class="pmc_sec_title">
<em>BASIC PROTOCOL 2:</em> Establishing human 3D cervical tissues using the rotating wall vessel bioreactor</h2>
<p id="P376">This protocol describes a method to generate physiologically relevant 3D tissues using innovative rotating wall vessel (RWV) bioreactor technology. Inside the RWV bioreactor, cells experience low physiological fluid shear conditions. The bioreactors come in two different formats, a high-aspect rotating vessel (HARV) or a slow-turning lateral vessel (STLV), in which they differ by their aeration source. Epithelial cells are mixed with collagen coated microbeads and added to the bioreactor. Following differentiation, the tissues can be harvested and used to study host-pathogen interactions. We provide details on how to culture HPV E6 and E7 immortalized, human cervical A2EN cells. However, with minor modifications, these methods can be used to create several three-dimensional (3D) cell culture models (i.e., vagina, gastrointestinal, lung, colon, placental, and neuronal) that exhibit physiologically relevant features observed <em>in vivo</em> (<a href="#R8" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R8">Carterson et al., 2005</a>; <a href="#R29" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R29">Hjelm et al., 2010</a>; <a href="#R30" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R30">Höner zu Bentrup et al., 2006</a>; <a href="#R38" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R38">LaMarca et al., 2005</a>; <a href="#R51" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R51">Myers et al., 2008</a>; <a href="#R52" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R52">Nickerson et al., 2001</a>).</p>
<p id="P377">The RWV bioreactor cell culture system provides a low fluid shear microenvironment that enables cells to form 3D cellular aggregates with <em>in vivo</em>-like characteristics, including tight junctions, mucin production, extracellular processes (i.e. microvilli), and cellular polarity.</p>
<section id="S50"><h3 class="pmc_sec_title">Materials</h3>
<section id="S51"><h4 class="pmc_sec_title">Reagents, solutions, and cell lines</h4>
<ul id="L110" class="list" style="list-style-type:none">
<li><p id="P378">Human endocervical EC line (A2EN)</p></li>
<li><p id="P379">Gibco Keratinocyte serum-free medium (1X), without calcium chloride (Thermo Scientific, cat. no. 37010022)</p></li>
<li><p id="P380">Invivogen Primocin, 50 mg/ml (Thermo Scientific, cat. no. NC9392943)</p></li>
<li><p id="P381">Invitrogen 0.4% Trypan blue solution (Fisher Scientific, cat. no. <a href="https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/nuccore/T10282" class="usa-link" data-ga-action="click_feat_suppl" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">T10282</a>)</p></li>
<li><p id="P382">70% Ethanol</p></li>
</ul></section><section id="S52"><h4 class="pmc_sec_title">Hardware and instruments</h4>
<ul id="L112" class="list" style="list-style-type:none">
<li><p id="P383">Prepared STLV BIOREACTOR</p></li>
<li><p id="P384">Prepared Cytodex-3 collagen-coated microcarrier beads</p></li>
<li><p id="P385">Sterile 5 ml Luer-lock syringes (Fisher Scientific, cat. no. 14-955-458)</p></li>
<li><p id="P386">Sterile 10 ml Luer-lock syringes (Fisher Scientific, cat. no. 14-955-459)</p></li>
<li><p id="P387">Inverted light microscope</p></li>
</ul></section></section><section id="S53"><h3 class="pmc_sec_title">Protocol steps</h3>
<p id="P388">Perform these procedures in a class II biosafety cabinet with laminar air flow.</p>
<p id="P389">This protocol is estimated to generate ~36 1 ml aliquots in two 24-well plates.</p>
<ul id="L114" class="list" style="list-style-type:none">
<li><p id="P390">1. Detach human A2EN cervical epithelial cells cultured as monolayers from Support Protocol 4 by trypsinization as outlined in <a href="#S34" class="usa-link">Support Protocol 4</a> and resuspend in 10 ml prewarmed complete KFSM medium. Add 10 μl of the cell suspension to a 0.5 ml microcentrifuge tube. Add 10 μl 0.4% trypan blue solution and mix gently by pipetting. Enumerate live cells by trypan blue exclusion staining.</p></li>
<li><p id="P391">2. Add 1×10<sup>7</sup> viable cells to the conical tube containing the prepared Cytodex-3 microcarrier beads. Carefully pour the A2EN cells and microcarrier beads into the STLV bioreactor through the central port. Seal the central port with the provided plug and incubate at 37°C, 5% CO<sub>2</sub> without rotation for 1 hour to allow A2EN cells to adhere to beads.</p></li>
<li><p id="P392">3. Remove plungers from the sterile syringes and resleeve plungers in their plastic wrapper to maintain sterility. Attach one 5 ml and one 10 ml syringe to the one-way stop cocks.</p></li>
<li><p id="P393">4. Open both stop cocks and fill the STLV bioreactor with complete KFSM medium through the 10 ml syringe.</p></li>
<li>
<p id="P394">5. Close the 5 ml syringe stop cock when the medium begins to flow into the syringe port. Continue filling with complete KFSM medium to the 10 ml syringe line. Insert both plungers and remove bubbles.
</p>
<p id="P395">It is important to ensure all bubbles are removed from the medium within the STLV to avoid mechanical shearing of the cells from the bead surface and to promote 3D A2EN cellular aggregate formation.</p>
</li>
<li><p id="P396">6. Attach the STLV bioreactor to the rotator unit housed inside a 37°C incubator. Turn on the power and adjust the rotational speed to 20 rpm.</p></li>
<li><p id="P397">5. Allow the STLV bioreactor to incubate at 37°C, 20 rpm for three days without changing the culture medium. Remove bubbles daily to maximize cell attachment to microcarrier beads and minimize disruption of 3D cellular aggregate formation.</p></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P398">6. On the <strong>fourth day of incubation</strong>, replace the spent culture medium from the STLV bioreactor.
<ol id="L116" class="list" style="list-style-type:lower-alpha">
<li><div class="p" id="P399">Open the stop cocks and remove both syringe plungers.</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P400">Tilt the STLV bioreactor so the 10 ml syringe side is at an ~45° angle and allow the 3D cell aggregates to settle in the corner.</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P401">Use a sterile 10 ml serological pipette attached to an automatic pipettor, to slowly aspirate and discard 40 ml of the spent culture medium. Avoid removing the 3D A2EN cellular aggregates.</div></li>
</ol>
</div></li>
<li><p id="P402">7. Unpackage new 5 ml and 10 ml syringes. Remove plungers and resleeve in their plastic wrapper to maintain sterility. Replace old syringes with new syringes.</p></li>
<li><p id="P403">8. Fill STLV bioreactor with fresh, prewarmed complete KFSM medium, as outlined in <strong>steps 4–5 above</strong>.</p></li>
<li>
<p id="P404">9. Reattach the STLV bioreactor to the rotating unit and resume incubation at 37°C, 20 rpm.
</p>
<p id="P405">The bioreactor must be incubated with continuous rotation, except when replacing culture medium and transferring 3D A2EN cellular aggregates to the disposable HARV.</p>
</li>
<li><p id="P406">10. Replace the culture medium every other day until day 10; after day 10, replace culture medium daily until day 28 of incubation.</p></li>
<li><p id="P407">11. Monitor development of the 3D A2EN cellular aggregates on a weekly basis by removing ~0.2 ml of resuspended A2EN cellular aggregates from the central port using a wide-bore 1000 μl pipette tip. Place 3D A2EN cellular aggregates in a small petri dish containing 0.5–1 ml of medium and visualize using an inverted light microscope.</p></li>
<li><p id="P408">12. After 21 days of incubation in the STLV bioreactor, unpackage a sterile disposable HARV bioreactor and remove the central plug.</p></li>
<li><p id="P409">12. Decontaminate the STLV surface with 70% ethanol and dry thoroughly.</p></li>
<li><p id="P410">13. Aspirate and discard 30 ml of spent culture medium from the STLV bioreactor.</p></li>
<li><p id="P411">14. Remove the central port plug and gently swirl the STLV bioreactor to resuspend the 3D A2EN cellular aggregates.</p></li>
<li><p id="P412">15. Carefully pour the mixture into a sterile 50 ml conical tube. Allow the 3D A2EN cellular aggregates to settle.</p></li>
<li><p id="P413">16. Aspirate and discard ~10 ml of the upper supernatant layer. Gently swirl the 50 ml conical tube to resuspend the 3D A2EN cellular aggregates.</p></li>
<li><p id="P414">17. Using a wide-bore 1000 μl pipette, carefully transfer the 3D A2EN cellular aggregates into the disposable HARV bioreactor through the central port.</p></li>
<li><p id="P415">18. Collect residual 3D A2EN cellular aggregates by rinsing the 50 ml conical tube walls with 10 ml of fresh prewarmed complete KFSM medium. Transfer residual 3D A2EN cellular aggregates to the HARV bioreactor and replace the central plug.</p></li>
<li>
<p id="P416">19. Unpackage new 5 ml and 10 ml syringes and remove plungers. Resleeve plungers in their plastic wrappers to maintain sterility. Attach syringes to the disposable HARV built-in stop cocks. Fill with prewarmed complete KFSM medium, as outlined in <strong>steps 4–5 above</strong>.
</p>
<p id="P417">It is important to ensure all bubbles are removed from the medium within the STLV to avoid mechanical shearing of the cells from the bead surface and to promote 3D A2EN cellular aggregate formation.</p>
</li>
<li><p id="P418">20. Attach the disposable HARV bioreactor to the rotator unit and incubate at 37°C, 20 rpm for 7 additional days. Replace medium daily, as outlined in <strong>step 4–5 above</strong>.</p></li>
<li><p id="P419">21. The 3D human A2EN cellular aggregates are ready to harvest for downstream experimentation on day 28 of incubation.</p></li>
<li><p id="P420">22. Remove syringe plungers and aspirate and discard ~30 ml of culture medium. Remove the central port from the HARV bioreactor, gently swirl to resuspend the 3D A2EN cellular aggregates, and carefully pour mixture into a sterile 50 ml conical tube.</p></li>
<li><p id="P421">23. Allow 3D A2EN cellular aggregates to settle. Aspirate 10 ml of the top layer of culture medium and add to the disposable HARV bioreactor.</p></li>
<li><p id="P422">24. Gently swirl the disposable HARV to collect residual 3D A2EN cellular aggregates and carefully pour into the 50 ml conical tube to pool the samples.</p></li>
<li><p id="P423">25. Allow the 3D A2EN cellular aggregates to settle.</p></li>
<li>
<p id="P424">26. Aspirate and discard the top layer of culture medium.
</p>
<p id="P425">Perform all remaining steps with KFSM medium without Primocin added.</p>
</li>
<li><p id="P426">27. Wash 3D A2EN cellular aggregates with 15 ml of KFSM medium without Primocin. Gently swirl tube to ensure 3D A2EN aggregates are thoroughly washed. Allow 3D A2EN cellular aggregates to settle.</p></li>
<li><p id="P427">28. Aspirate and discard the upper layer of medium. Repeat rinse with ~40 ml of KFSM medium lacking Primocin. Allow 3D A2EN cellular aggregates to settle.</p></li>
<li>
<p id="P428">29. Swirl 50 ml conical tube to thoroughly resuspend 3D A2EN cellular aggregates. Using a wide-bore 1000 μl pipette tip, aliquot 1 ml samples into a sterile 24-well tissue-treated culture plate.
</p>
<p id="P429">It is important to thoroughly resuspend 3D cellular aggregates before each 1 ml aliquot to ensure 3D A2EN cellular aggregates are evenly partitioned amongst the 24-well plate.</p>
</li>
