<li><p id="P430">30. Halfway through the aliquot process (after transferring to 18 wells), transfer 1 ml of 3D A2EN cellular aggregates to a sterile 1.5 ml microcentrifuge tube for enumerating 3D A2EN cells by trypan blue exclusion.</p></li>
<li><p id="P431">31. Incubate the 1.5 ml microfuge tube containing 3D A2EN cellular aggregates at 37°C and continue aliquoting 3D A2EN cellular aggregates into the remaining wells of both 24-well plates. When complete, incubate both 24-well plates at 37°C, 5% CO<sub>2</sub>.</p></li>
<li><p id="P432">32. The 3D A2EN cellular aggregates are now ready to be used for downstream assays.</p></li>
<li><p id="P433">33. To count the cells, aspirate and discard the upper layer of culture medium from the 1.5 ml microcentrifuge tube containing 3D A2EN cellular aggregates from <strong>step 30</strong>. Avoid transferring the 3D A2EN cellular aggregates. Wash the 3D A2EN cellular aggregates with 1 ml of sterile D-PBS pre-warmed to 37°C. Allow the 3D A2EN cellular aggregates to settle.</p></li>
<li><p id="P434">34. Aspirate and discard the upper layer of D-PBS, being careful not to remove the 3D A2EN cellular aggregates.</p></li>
<li>
<p id="P435">35. Treat the 3D A2EN cellular aggregates with 300 μl of pre-warmed trypsin-EDTA to dissociate the 3D A2EN cells from the microcarrier bead matrix. Invert the tube several times to mix thoroughly. Incubate the 3D A2EN cellular aggregates at 37°C for 10 minutes with periodic inversion to promote detachment.
</p>
<p id="P436">The beads will progressively look like “particles of sand” as the 3D A2EN cells dissociate from the microcarrier beads with continued incubation in the trypsin-EDTA solution.</p>
</li>
<li><p id="P437">36. Add pre-warmed neutralization medium to the 1.5 ml microfuge tube to the 1 ml gradient line (~500–600 μl). Mix thoroughly by inverting the tube several times. Allow the microcarrier beads to settle.</p></li>
<li><p id="P438">37. Aspirate 10 μl of the A2EN cell-containing supernatant into a sterile 0.5 ml microcentrifuge tube. Add 10 μl of 0.4% trypan blue solution and gently mix by pipetting. Enumerate viable cells using an automated cell counter (e.g., Invitrogen Countess) or manually using a hemocytometer, according to the manufacturer’s instructions.</p></li>
<li><p id="P439">38. Utilize 3D A2EN cellular aggregates incubating in the 24-well plates for downstream experimental analysis.</p></li>
</ul>
<p id="P440">A workflow diagram for generating 3D A2EN cells is shown in <a href="#F4" class="usa-link">Fig. 4</a>.</p>
<figure class="fig xbox font-sm" id="F4"><h4 class="obj_head">Figure 4.</h4>
<p class="img-box line-height-none margin-x-neg-2 tablet:margin-x-0 text-center"><img class="graphic" src="https://cdn.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/blobs/3a7a/11088941/0b121a467792/nihms-1991549-f0004.jpg" loading="lazy" height="1920" width="1414" alt="Figure 4"></p>
<div class="p text-right font-secondary"><a href="figure/F4/" class="usa-link" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Open in a new tab</a></div>
<figcaption><p id="P788">Workflow diagram for generating 3D A2EN cells using RWV bioreactor technology. Downstream experimental procedures for utilizing 3D A2EN cells includes, but is not limited to, infection with bacteria or viruses, investigating compound cytotoxicity, and ultrastructural imaging using scanning electron microscopy or transmission electron microscopy.</p></figcaption></figure></section></section><section id="S54"><h2 class="pmc_sec_title">
<em>BASIC PROTOCOL 3:</em> Histological assessment of 3D organotypic raft tissues</h2>
<p id="P441">The methods outlined in <a href="#S22" class="usa-link">Basic Protocol 1</a> aim to generate tissues that accurately represent the original tissue. Routine histological assessment on formalin-fixed paraffin-embedded tissue sections usually involves staining with haematoxylin and eosin (H&amp;E) staining. This allows for visualization of organotypic cultures. Comparison with known tissues, e.g., through the Human Protein Atlas (<a href="http://www.proteinatlas.org" class="usa-link usa-link--external" data-ga-action="click_feat_suppl" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">http://www.proteinatlas.org</a>, see the Normal Tissue Histology section of the Dictionary; <a href="#R67" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R67">Uhlén et al., 2005</a>), will allow for comparison between the organotypic tissues and their <em>in vivo</em> counterparts. Finally, histological assessment can be the first step in observing any morphological changes related to your experiment.</p>
<p id="P442">Methods for tissue embedding, sectioning, and H&amp;E staining are beyond the scope of this protocol. We provide details on methods that will allow the reader to identify epithelial strata in their cultures, compare these structures to genuine tissues, and ultimately determine the success of their raft cultures.</p>
<section id="S55"><h3 class="pmc_sec_title">Materials</h3>
<p id="P443">H&amp;E stained slides with permanently mounted coverslip (rafts should be cut in half, bisected, and embedded so that the open faces are orientated to allow a cross-sectional view of the epithelium, 4 μm thickness, two sections per slide)</p>
<p id="P444">Microscope with color camera</p></section><section id="S56"><h3 class="pmc_sec_title">Protocol Steps</h3>
<ol id="L118" class="list" style="list-style-type:decimal">
<li><p id="P445">Observe the entire epithelium for each tissue piece for histological features.</p></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P446">Ensure that the two major compartments are present: dermis (or stroma) and epidermis (or epithelium, proper).
<ol id="L120" class="list" style="list-style-type:lower-alpha">
<li><div class="p" id="P447">The dermis should appear light pink (eosin-stained collagen fibers) with sporadic dark purple/blue, haematoxylin-stained fibroblast nuclei.</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P448">Observe the clear distinction between the dermal compartment and the epidermis (darker pink, more nuclei, stratified keratinocytes).</div></li>
<li>
<div class="p" id="P449">The epidermis of full-thickness stratified squamous epithelium should consist of a basal layer of proliferating keratinocytes (<em>stratum basale</em>), with a basement membrane dividing this layer from the dermis. Cells above the basal layer are referred to as “suprabasal” and comprise several strata making up an intermediate “midzone” and then at the top a “superficial” layer. The cells immediately above the basal layer are referred to as “parabasal”, whereas the majority of midzone cells make up the <em>stratum spinosum</em>. Above the spinous layer is a thin granular layer (<em>stratum granulosum</em>) and then the <em>stratum lucidum</em> and finally the <em>stratum corneum</em> (which is predominantly present in keratinizing epithelia, like cutaneous skin, making up the uppermost and most differentiated superficial cells, and absent or only partially present in non-keratinizing mucosal epithelia, like tonsillar or ectocervical tissue.
</div>
<div class="p" id="P450">Occasionally upper layers of the epidermis, or even the entire epidermis itself, can detach during raft harvesting or tissue processing. These pieces may still be stained and observable, so if you see only dermis in the main tissue piece make sure you look around the area (at low magnification, like 10x) to see if the epidermal compartment is nearby.</div>
</li>
</ol>
</div></li>
</ol>
<p id="P451">Example histology data are shown in <a href="#F5" class="usa-link">Fig. 5</a>.</p>
<figure class="fig xbox font-sm" id="F5"><h4 class="obj_head">Figure 5.</h4>
<p class="img-box line-height-none margin-x-neg-2 tablet:margin-x-0 text-center"><img class="graphic" src="https://cdn.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/blobs/3a7a/11088941/387eaef5a8fc/nihms-1991549-f0005.jpg" loading="lazy" height="1920" width="1501" alt="Figure 5"></p>
<div class="p text-right font-secondary"><a href="figure/F5/" class="usa-link" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Open in a new tab</a></div>
<figcaption><p id="P789">Histological microscope images of 3D organotypic epithelia. Hematoxylin and eosin (H&amp;E) stained cross-sections of 3D rafts grown from (A) HPV18 negative (top) and positive (bottom) human cervical keratinocytes and (B) human tonsillar keratinocytes clearly show stratified squamous epithelial structure. Different layers of the organotypic epithelia are marked with arrows.</p></figcaption></figure></section></section><section id="S57"><h2 class="pmc_sec_title">
<em>BASIC PROTOCOL 4:</em> Spatial analysis of protein expression in 3D organotypic raft cultures</h2>
<p id="P452">While H&amp;E stained tissues provide a general idea of the histological features of these 3D cultures (Basic Protocol 3), this stain does not provide data on specific proteins that have unique expression patterns between different tissues, spatially according to the differentiation state of the tissue, or dysregulated as a result of viral activities. This protocol provides methods to characterize target proteins in 3D raft tissue using immunofluorescence on formalin-fixed paraffin embedded tissue sections. The conditions used here work for detecting differentiation (e.g., keratins) and viral life cycle related markers (e.g., dysregulated cell cycle proteins, such as p16), but the reader should keep in mind that conditions (e.g., as antigen-retrieval, blocking buffer composition, and antibody dilutions) may need to be optimized for a specific target of interests.</p>
<section id="S58"><h3 class="pmc_sec_title">Materials</h3>
<section id="S59"><h4 class="pmc_sec_title">Reagents, solutions, and cell lines</h4>
<ul id="L122" class="list" style="list-style-type:none">
<li><p id="P453">Formalin-fixed paraffin embedded unstained tissue sections on microscope slides</p></li>
<li><p id="P454">Xylenes</p></li>
<li><p id="P455">100% EtOH</p></li>
<li><p id="P456">10mM Citrate buffer pH 6 (or, alternatively, optimal antigen-retrieval buffer)</p></li>
<li><p id="P457">1X phosphate buffered saline (PBS, from 10x stock, see recipe)</p></li>
<li><p id="P458">Bovine serum albumin (Bioworld, cat. no. 22070023–2)</p></li>
<li><p id="P459">2% BSA/PBS block or equivalent</p></li>
<li><p id="P460">Tween-20 (Fisher Scientific, cat. no. BP337–500)</p></li>
<li><p id="P461">Mouse anti-human KRT10 monoclonal antibody (clone DE-K10, ThermoFisher Scientific, cat. no. MA5–13705, 0.2 mg/ml stock concentration)</p></li>
<li><p id="P462">Mouse anti-human p16INK4A monoclonal antibody (clone JC8, Santa Cruz Biotechnologies, cat. no. sc-56330, 0.2 mg/ml stock concentration)</p></li>
<li><p id="P463">Goat anti-Mouse IgG (H+L) Highly Cross-Adsorbed Secondary Antibody, Alexa Fluor 488 (green, ThermoFisher Scientific, cat. no. A-11029)</p></li>
<li><p id="P464">Goat anti-Mouse IgG (H+L) Highly Cross-Adsorbed Secondary Antibody, Alexa Fluor 555 (red, ThermoFisher Scientific, cat. no. A-21424)</p></li>
<li><p id="P465">ProLong Gold antifade reagent with 4′,6-diamidino-2-phenylindole (Molecular Probes, Invitrogen).</p></li>
</ul></section><section id="S60"><h4 class="pmc_sec_title">Hardware and instruments</h4>
<ul id="L124" class="list" style="list-style-type:none">
<li><p id="P466">Coplin jar or equivalent</p></li>
<li><p id="P467">Chemical fume hood</p></li>
<li><p id="P468">Delicate task kimwipes</p></li>
<li><p id="P469">Steamer (KLARSTEIN Electric Food Steamer, 1500 W) or pressure cooker</p></li>
<li><p id="P470">Barrier pen or wax pencil</p></li>
<li><p id="P471">Glass Coverslips</p></li>
<li><p id="P472">Cardboard slide book for storage</p></li>
<li><p id="P473">Humidified staining chamber</p></li>
</ul></section></section><section id="S61"><h3 class="pmc_sec_title">Protocol steps</h3>
<section id="S62"><h4 class="pmc_sec_title">Day #1</h4>
<ul id="L126" class="list" style="list-style-type:none">
<li>
<span class="label">1</span><div class="display-inline p" id="P474">In a fume hood, deparaffinize the tissue slides (from Basic Protocol 1, Step 34c) using xylenes
<ol id="L128" class="list" style="list-style-type:lower-alpha"><li><div class="p" id="P475">Incubate 3 × 10 min, in covered glass Coplin jar in fume hood (move slides up/down 10x at start of each incubation)</div></li></ol>
</div>
</li>
<li>
<span class="label">2</span><div class="display-inline p" id="P476">In a fume hood, wash deparaffinized slides with 100% EtOH
<ol id="L130" class="list" style="list-style-type:lower-alpha"><li><div class="p" id="P477">Incubate 3 × 5 min, in covered glass Coplin jar in a fume hood (move slides up/down 10x at start of each incubation)</div></li></ol>
</div>
</li>
<li>
<span class="label">3</span><p class="display-inline" id="P478">Rinse slides twice using ddH<sub>2</sub>O</p>
</li>
<li>
<span class="label">4</span><div class="display-inline p" id="P479">Cover the slides with 10 mM citrate buffer in a heat-safe plastic Coplin jar (or equivalent container with slide rack), keeping the lid loose.
<ol id="L132" class="list" style="list-style-type:lower-alpha"><li><div class="p" id="P480">Specific antigens may require optimal antigen-retrieval buffers. Often, this information is available in datasheets but otherwise needs to be determined experimentally.</div></li></ol>
</div>
</li>
<li>
<span class="label">5</span><div class="display-inline p" id="P481">Incubate the slides in a steamer for 30 min (preset 5 of 7), then allow to cool for 20 min.
<ol id="L134" class="list" style="list-style-type:lower-alpha"><li><div class="p" id="P482">Other epitope retrieval methods are likely appropriate but will need to be optimized to maximize signal to background for desired antigen using appropriate controls.</div></li></ol>
</div>
</li>
<li>
<span class="label">6</span><div class="display-inline p" id="P483">Rinse slides twice in ddH<sub>2</sub>O.
<ol id="L136" class="list" style="list-style-type:lower-alpha"><li><div class="p" id="P484">Ensure that excess liquid is removed.</div></li></ol>
</div>
</li>
<li>
<span class="label">7</span><p class="display-inline" id="P485">Draw hydrophobic circles around tissue sections using a barrier pen or wax pencil</p>
</li>
<li>
<span class="label">8</span><p class="display-inline" id="P486">Rinse the slide in 1x PBS.</p>
</li>
<li>
<span class="label">9</span><div class="display-inline p" id="P487">Incubate the slides in 2% BSA/PBS block for 30 minutes.
<ol id="L138" class="list" style="list-style-type:lower-alpha">
<li><div class="p" id="P488">Ensure enough volume to fully cover the tissue section (with tightly drawn hydrophobic circles around typical bisected raft tissue we find 100 μl enough to cover). If needed, rotate the slide to ensure the drop fills the entire tissue section, gently tap while rotating if needed, ensuring the volume doesn’t leak past the barrier (if it does, add additional volume). If you’re having issues with tissue sections not being fully covered: add a surfactant such as Tween-20 (0.05% final concentration) to your buffers and diluents, which will help break the surface tension and allow tissue sections to be fully covered. (Addition of detergent may affect the staining).</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P489">In our hands, a 2% BSA/PBS block is sufficient in most cases, but consider a normal sera block if you are observing high background due to non-specific secondary antibody binding.</div></li>
</ol>
</div>
</li>
<li>
<span class="label">10</span><p class="display-inline" id="P490">Dilute the primary antibody at appropriate dilution/concentration (1:100, 2 μg/ml final concentration, for both anti-KRT10 and anti-p16), in the blocking buffer (e.g., 2% BSA/PBS).</p>
</li>
<li>
<span class="label">11</span><p class="display-inline" id="P491">Shake off blocking buffer. Carefully place the slides flat in a humidified staining chamber and add 100 μl diluted primary antibody. Include a no-primary antibody control (blocking buffer only) for assessing non-specific secondary antibody signal. Incubate overnight in the fridge at 4°C.</p>
</li>
</ul></section><section id="S63"><h4 class="pmc_sec_title">Day #2</h4>
<ul id="L140" class="list" style="list-style-type:none">
<li>
<span class="label">12</span><p class="display-inline" id="P492">Rinse slides using 1x PBS</p>
</li>
<li>
<span class="label">13</span><p class="display-inline" id="P493">Incubate slides in 1x PBS for 5 minutes at room temperature</p>
</li>
<li>
<span class="label">14</span><p class="display-inline" id="P494">Repeat step 13 for a total of three washes</p>
</li>
<li>
<span class="label">15</span><div class="display-inline p" id="P495">Add secondary antibody conjugates to fluorophores made up in diluent (1:800, 1.25 μg/ml final)
<ol id="L142" class="list" style="list-style-type:lower-alpha">
<li><div class="p" id="P496">Use the same method as described for the primary antibodies (step 9 to 11, above)</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P497">Incubate for 30 min at room temperature protected from light</div></li>
</ol>
</div>
</li>
<li>
<span class="label">16</span><p class="display-inline" id="P498">Rinse slides using 1x PBS</p>
</li>
<li>
<span class="label">17</span><p class="display-inline" id="P499">Incubate slides in 1x PBS for 5 minutes at room temperature</p>
</li>
<li>
<span class="label">18</span><p class="display-inline" id="P500">Repeat step 17 for a total of three washes</p>
</li>
<li>
<span class="label">19</span><div class="display-inline p" id="P501">Rinse slides twice in ddH<sub>2</sub>O.
<ol id="L144" class="list" style="list-style-type:lower-alpha"><li><div class="p" id="P502">Ensure that excess liquid is removed, but do not dry completely.</div></li></ol>
</div>
</li>
<li>
<span class="label">20</span><p class="display-inline" id="P503">Mount w/ DAPI-containing mounting media, one drop per section (~25 μl), enough to cover tissue area.</p>
</li>
<li>
<span class="label">21</span><div class="display-inline p" id="P504">Coverslip with 1.5 thickness coverglass 22×50 full-length, ensure no bubbles.
<ol id="L146" class="list" style="list-style-type:lower-alpha"><li><div class="p" id="P505">Coverslip can be removed if needed by placing the slide in a Coplin jar containing 1x PBS and letting the coverslip fall off naturally, so tissue is not damaged.</div></li></ol>
</div>
</li>
<li>
<span class="label">22</span><p class="display-inline" id="P506">Store slides protected from light and allow curing mountant to cure.</p>
</li>
<li>
<span class="label">23</span><p class="display-inline" id="P507">Store slides at 4°C or room temp afterward, depending on the mountant used.</p>
</li>
<li>
<span class="label">24</span><p class="display-inline" id="P508">Image slides using a fluorescence microscope.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p id="P509">Example immunofluorescence data are shown in <a href="#F6" class="usa-link">Fig. 6</a>.</p>
<figure class="fig xbox font-sm" id="F6"><h5 class="obj_head">Figure 6.</h5>
<p class="img-box line-height-none margin-x-neg-2 tablet:margin-x-0 text-center"><img class="graphic" src="https://cdn.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/blobs/3a7a/11088941/efbd6521169e/nihms-1991549-f0006.jpg" loading="lazy" height="1920" width="1820" alt="Figure 6"></p>
<div class="p text-right font-secondary"><a href="figure/F6/" class="usa-link" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Open in a new tab</a></div>
<figcaption><p id="P790">Immunofluorescence images of 3D organotypic rafts depicting protein-level confirmation of (A, B) differentiation marker keratin 10 (KRT10) and (C) HPV-induced host cell cycle dysregulation marker p16<sup>INK4A</sup>. In panel A, KRT10 (red cytoplasmic signal) is expressed in suprabasal differentiated cells, in only the uppermost layers in cervical and tonsillar-derived 3D rafts, compared to all suprabasal cells in foreskin-derived 3D rafts as a control. The white dotted line indicates the transition from dermis to epidermis. Differential staining of cytokeratins highlights the differences between tissues derived from unique anatomic sites, such as non-keratinizing epithelium of the oral mucosa and cervix compared to keratinizing epithelium of the foreskin. Importantly, Basic Protocol 1 yields 3D organotypic raft tissues that resemble the anatomic site of origin dependent on the primary keratinocytes used. Reference images are from the Human Protein Atlas (HPA, available from <a href="http://www.proteinatlas.org" class="usa-link usa-link--external" data-ga-action="click_feat_suppl" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">http://www.proteinatlas.org</a>, <a href="#R67" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R67">Uhlén et al., 2005</a>) with immunohistochemical stain (DAB, brown) for KRT10 (ENSG00000186395): normal skin tissue (T-01000, Skin 1, CAB000132, Male, age 63, Patient id: 2418), normal cervical tissue (T-83000, HPA012014, Female, age 37, Patient id: 4504), and normal tonsil tissue (T-61100, CAB000132, Male, age 31, Patient id: 2511). An enlarged view of KRT10-stained tonsillar raft tissue is shown in panel B, corresponding to the white-dotted box. In panel C, p16<sup>INK4A</sup> (red) is over-expressed in HPV-positive tissues, with stronger and more diffuse cytoplasmic staining as a signature of HPV-induced changes within host cells. Cell nuclei are DAPI-stained (blue) and the basal layer of keratinocytes are visually separated from the underlying dermis (containing fibroblasts embedded in collagen) by a white-dotted line.</p></figcaption></figure></section></section></section><section id="S64"><h2 class="pmc_sec_title">
<em>BASIC PROTOCOL 5:</em> Immunofluorescent microscopy imaging of rotating wall vessel derived 3D tissues</h2>
<p id="P510">Similar to the method described in <a href="#S57" class="usa-link">Basic Protocol 4</a>, this protocol describes a method to identify specific proteins and their expression patterns in the 3D RWV derived tissues.</p>
<section id="S65"><h3 class="pmc_sec_title">Materials</h3>
<section id="S66"><h4 class="pmc_sec_title">Reagents, solutions, and cell lines</h4>
<ul id="L148" class="list" style="list-style-type:none">
<li><p id="P511">3D tissue aggregates generated in <a href="#S49" class="usa-link">Basic Protocol 2</a></p></li>
<li><p id="P512">1X phosphate buffered saline (PBS, from 10x stock, see recipe)</p></li>
<li><p id="P513">4% formaldehyde in 1x PBS (Electron Microscopy Sciences, cat. no. 15710)</p></li>
<li><p id="P514">0.5% Triton X-100 in 1x PBS (Electron Microscopy Sciences, cat. no. 22140)</p></li>
<li><p id="P515">Bovine serum albumin (BSA; Bioworld, cat. no. 22070023–2)</p></li>
<li><p id="P516">8% BSA diluted in 1x PBS</p></li>
<li><p id="P517">Mouse anti-human KRT10 monoclonal antibody (clone DE-K10, ThermoFisher Scientific, cat. no. MA5–13705, 0.2 mg/ml stock concentration)</p></li>
<li><p id="P518">Mouse anti-human p16INK4A monoclonal antibody (clone JC8, Santa Cruz Biotechnologies, cat. no. sc-56330, 0.2 mg/ml stock concentration)</p></li>
<li><p id="P519">Goat anti-Mouse IgG (H+L) Highly Cross-Adsorbed Secondary Antibody, Alexa Fluor 488 (green, ThermoFisher Scientific, cat. no. A-11029)</p></li>
<li><p id="P520">Goat anti-Mouse IgG (H+L) Highly Cross-Adsorbed Secondary Antibody, Alexa Fluor 555 (red, ThermoFisher Scientific, cat. no. A-21424)</p></li>
<li><p id="P521">0.1% Tween 20 (VWR) in PBS (T-PBS)</p></li>
<li><p id="P522">ProLong Gold antifade reagent with 4′,6-diamidino-2-phenylindole (Molecular Probes, Invitrogen, cat. no. <a href="https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/protein/P36931" class="usa-link" data-ga-action="click_feat_suppl" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">P36931</a>)</p></li>
</ul></section><section id="S67"><h4 class="pmc_sec_title">Hardware and instruments</h4>
<ul id="L150" class="list" style="list-style-type:none">
<li><p id="P523">1.5 ml centrifuge tubes</p></li>
<li><p id="P524">centrifuge</p></li>
<li><p id="P525">Glass Coverslips</p></li>
<li><p id="P526">Cardboard slide book for storage</p></li>
</ul></section></section><section id="S68"><h3 class="pmc_sec_title">Protocol steps</h3>
<ol id="L152" class="list" style="list-style-type:decimal">
<li><p id="P527">Transfer ~100 μl aggregates to a 1.5 ml tube</p></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P528">Wash aggregates using 1x PBS
<ol id="L154" class="list" style="list-style-type:lower-alpha"><li><div class="p" id="P529">allow aggregates to settle in between washes</div></li></ol>
</div></li>
<li><p id="P530">Add 200 μl 4% formaldehyde and incubate 30 minutes at room temperature</p></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P531">Wash aggregates using 1x PBS
<ol id="L156" class="list" style="list-style-type:lower-alpha"><li><div class="p" id="P532">allow aggregates to settle in between washes</div></li></ol>
</div></li>
<li><p id="P533">Repeat step 4 for a total of 3 washes</p></li>
<li><p id="P534">Add 200 μl 0.5% Triton X-100 to permeabilize the cells</p></li>
<li><p id="P535">incubate 5 minutes at room temperature</p></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P536">Wash aggregates using 1x PBS
<ol id="L158" class="list" style="list-style-type:lower-alpha"><li><div class="p" id="P537">allow aggregates to settle in between washes</div></li></ol>
</div></li>
<li><p id="P538">Repeat step 8 for a total of 3 washes</p></li>
<li><p id="P539">Add 200 μl 8% BSA to block non-specific binding</p></li>
<li><p id="P540">Incubate 1 hour at 37°C</p></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P541">Wash aggregates using 1x PBS
<ol id="L160" class="list" style="list-style-type:lower-alpha"><li><div class="p" id="P542">allow aggregates to settle in between washes</div></li></ol>
</div></li>
<li><p id="P543">Repeat step 12 for a total of 3 washes</p></li>
<li><p id="P544">Dilute the primary antibody at appropriate dilution/concentration (1:100, 2 μg/ml final concentration, for both anti-KRT10 and anti-p16), in the blocking buffer (e.g., 8% BSA/PBS).</p></li>
<li><p id="P545">Incubate cells and primary antibody for 2 hours at 37°C (or overnight at 4°C)</p></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P546">Wash aggregates using PBS-T
<ol id="L162" class="list" style="list-style-type:lower-alpha"><li><div class="p" id="P547">allow aggregates to settle in between washes</div></li></ol>
</div></li>
<li><p id="P548">Repeat step 16 for a total of 3 washes</p></li>
<li><p id="P549">Dilute the appropriate fluorophore-conjugated secondary antibody at appropriate dilution/concentration (e.g., 1:500) in the blocking buffer (e.g., 8% BSA/PBS)</p></li>
<li><p id="P550">Incubate cells and secondary antibody for 1 hour at 37°C</p></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P551">Wash aggregates using PBS-T
<ol id="L164" class="list" style="list-style-type:lower-alpha"><li><div class="p" id="P552">allow aggregates to settle in between washes</div></li></ol>
</div></li>
<li><p id="P553">Repeat step 16 for a total of 3 washes</p></li>
<li><p id="P554">Rinse aggregates once with ddH2O</p></li>
<li><p id="P555">Place 1 drop of mounting media on microscope slide</p></li>
<li><p id="P556">Transfer labeled aggregates on top of mounting media with a cut-off 1000 μl pipette tip</p></li>
<li><p id="P557">place coverslip over aggregates</p></li>
<li><p id="P558">Cure slide overnight</p></li>
</ol></section></section><section id="S69"><h2 class="pmc_sec_title">
<em>BASIC PROTOCOL 6:</em> Ultrastructural visualization and imaging of rotating wall vessel derived 3D tissues</h2>
<p id="P559">The use of scanning electron microscopy allows researchers to visualize macromolecular structures and organelles. This approach allows for the unbiased visualization of surface characteristics and secretory vesicles/mucus deposits between adjacent cells and on the apical cell surface. These methods provide further characterization of the 3D models.</p>
<section id="S70"><h3 class="pmc_sec_title">Materials</h3>
<section id="S71"><h4 class="pmc_sec_title">Reagents, solutions, and cell lines</h4>
<ul id="L166" class="list" style="list-style-type:none">
<li><p id="P560">3D RWV-derived A2EN cervical cell aggregates generated in <a href="#S49" class="usa-link">Basic Protocol 2</a></p></li>
<li><p id="P561">8% glutaraldehyde solution (Electron Microscopy Sciences, cat. no. 16220)</p></li>
<li><p id="P562">Dubecco’s phosphate-buffered saline, 1X (Fisher Scientific, cat. no. MT21031CV)</p></li>
<li><p id="P563">4% Osmium tetroxide solution (Electron Microscopy Sciences, cat. no. 19410)</p></li>
<li><p id="P564">20% EtOH</p></li>
<li><p id="P565">50% EtOH</p></li>
<li><p id="P566">75% EtOH</p></li>
<li><p id="P567">95% EtOH</p></li>
<li><p id="P568">100% EtOH</p></li>
</ul></section><section id="S72"><h4 class="pmc_sec_title">Hardware and instruments</h4>
<ul id="L168" class="list" style="list-style-type:none">
<li><p id="P569">1.5 ml microcentrifuge tubes</p></li>
<li><p id="P570">Wide-bore 1000 μl pipette tips (cut ~0.5” from the tip and autoclaved to sterilize)</p></li>
<li><p id="P571">Disposable transfer pipette (Fisher Scientific, cat. no.</p></li>
<li><p id="P572">Critical point dryer</p></li>
<li><p id="P573">SEM specimen mount (Electron Microscopy Sciences, cat. no. 7550)</p></li>
<li><p id="P574">Conductive carbon adhesive tabs (Electron Microscopy Sciences, cat. no. 77825–12)</p></li>
<li><p id="P575">Sputter Coater</p></li>
<li><p id="P576">Scanning electron microscope</p></li>
</ul></section></section><section id="S73"><h3 class="pmc_sec_title">Protocol steps</h3>
<section id="S74"><h4 class="pmc_sec_title">Fixation of 3D A2EN cervical cells in glutaraldehyde</h4>
<ol id="L170" class="list" style="list-style-type:decimal">
<li><div class="p" id="P577">Generate 10 ml of 2.5% glutaraldehyde solution in sterile D-PBS from the 8% glutaraldehyde stock. Cover tube in foil and store at 4°C until further use.
<ol id="L172" class="list" style="list-style-type:lower-alpha"><li><div class="p" id="P578">Use 2.5% glutaraldehyde within 2 weeks storage or prepare a fresh solution from the 8% glutaraldehyde stock.</div></li></ol>
</div></li>
<li><p id="P579">Immediately after the 28 day differentiation period or post-infection, transfer the 3D A2EN cervical cell aggregates (see Basic Protocol 2, Step 38) and supernatant from one well of the 24-well plate to a 1.5 ml microcentrifuge tube using a wide-bore 1000 μl pipette tip.</p></li>
<li><p id="P580">Allow aggregates to settle to the bottom of the tube and aspirate the supernatant using a standard-bore 1000 μl pipette tip. Be careful not to remove the 3D A2EN cervical cell aggregates when removing supernatant.</p></li>
<li><p id="P581">Rinse the 3D A2EN cervical cell aggregates with 1X sterile D-PBS. Gently invert the tube several times to mix thoroughly. Allow the aggregates to settle to the bottom of the tube.</p></li>
<li><p id="P582">Aspirate the supernatant and repeat the wash from step 4.</p></li>
<li><p id="P583">Remove the supernatant and add fix the 3D A2EN cervical cell aggregates with 500 μl of 2.5% glutaraldehyde solution. Gently invert the tube several times to mix thoroughly.</p></li>
<li><p id="P584">Incubate the 3D A2EN cervical cells aggregates at room temperature for 30 minutes. Gently invert or flick the tube periodically to ensure complete fixation.</p></li>
<li><p id="P585">Transfer the 3D A2EN cervical cells suspended in 2.5% glutaraldehyde to a 4°C fridge and incubate overnight.</p></li>
<li><p id="P586">The next day, remove and discard the supernatant in an appropriate receptacle for glutaraldehyde waste. Rinse the fixed 3D A2EN cervical cell aggregates with 1 ml sterile D-PBS. Gently invert the tube to mix thoroughly. and allow the aggregates to settle to the bottom of the tube.</p></li>
<li><p id="P587">Aspirate the supernatant and repeat the rinse procedure 2X.</p></li>
<li><p id="P588">Suspend the 3D A2EN cervical cell aggregates in 1 ml sterile D-PBS. Store at 4°C until further use (cells may be stored up to 1 month under these conditions).</p></li>
</ol></section><section id="S75"><h4 class="pmc_sec_title">Scanning electron microscopy of 3D A2EN cervical cell aggregates</h4>
<ol id="L174" class="list" style="list-style-type:decimal">
<li><p id="P589">Prepare a 1% osmium tetroxide solution in 1X D-PBS. You will need 1 ml per sample being processed for SEM imaging.</p></li>
<li><p id="P590">Aspirate the D-PBS supernatant from the 1.5 ml tube containing the 3D A2EN cervical cell aggregates.</p></li>
<li><p id="P591">Rinse the 3D A2EN cervical cell aggregates in 1 ml D-PBS. Invert the tube several times to mix thoroughly. Incubate the sample at room temperature for 7–8 minutes.</p></li>
<li><p id="P592">Aspirate the supernatant and repeat the rinse with 1 ml D-PBS 3X.</p></li>
<li><p id="P593">Aspirate the supernatant and add 1 ml of 1% osmium tetroxide solution. Invert the tube several times to mix thoroughly. Incubate at room temperature for 1 hour.</p></li>
<li><p id="P594">Remove the supernatant rinse the 3D A2EN cervical cell aggregates in 1 ml dH<sub>2</sub>O. Invert the tube several times to mix thoroughly. Incubate at room temperature for 7–8 minutes.</p></li>
<li><p id="P595">Aspirate the supernatant and repeat the dH<sub>2</sub>O rinse 4X.</p></li>
<li><p id="P596">Aspirate the supernatant and add 1 ml of 20% EtOH to dehydrate the samples. Invert the tube several times to mix thoroughly. Incubate at room temperature for 8–10 minutes.</p></li>
<li><p id="P597">Aspirate the supernatant and add 1 ml of 50% EtOH to dehydrate the samples. Invert the tube several times to mix thoroughly. Incubate at room temperature for 8–10 minutes.</p></li>
<li><p id="P598">Aspirate the supernatant and add 1 ml of 75% EtOH to dehydrate the samples. Invert the tube several times to mix thoroughly. Incubate at room temperature for 8–10 minutes.</p></li>
<li><p id="P599">Aspirate the supernatant and add 1 ml of 95% EtOH to dehydrate the samples. Invert the tube several times to mix thoroughly. Incubate at room temperature for 8–10 minutes.</p></li>
<li><p id="P600">Aspirate the supernatant and add 1 ml of 100% EtOH to dehydrate the samples. Invert the tube several times to mix thoroughly. Incubate at room temperature for 8–10 minutes.</p></li>
<li><p id="P601">Aspirate the supernatant and repeat the dehydration process in 100% EtOH 2X.</p></li>
<li><p id="P602">Complete the drying process in a critical point dryer according to the manufacturer’s instructions.</p></li>
<li><p id="P603">Carefully transfer the samples to a SEM specimen mount containing a conductive carbon adhesive disk. Do not overload the specimen mount with too many 3D A2EN cervical cell aggregates.</p></li>
<li><p id="P604">Transfer the specimen mounts to a sputter coater and coat with thin-layer of PdAu according to the manufacturer’s instructions.</p></li>
<li><p id="P605">Visualize and image specimens using a scanning electron microscope.</p></li>
</ol>
<p id="P6005">Sample scanning electron microscopy data are shown in <a href="#F7" class="usa-link">Fig. 7</a>.</p>
<figure class="fig xbox font-sm" id="F7"><h5 class="obj_head">Figure 7.</h5>
<p class="img-box line-height-none margin-x-neg-2 tablet:margin-x-0 text-center"><img class="graphic" src="https://cdn.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/blobs/3a7a/11088941/43819b6606ad/nihms-1991549-f0007.jpg" loading="lazy" height="944" width="1920" alt="Figure 7"></p>
<div class="p text-right font-secondary"><a href="figure/F7/" class="usa-link" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Open in a new tab</a></div>
<figcaption><p id="P791">Scanning electron microscopy (SEM) of 3D A2EN cervical cell aggregates. 3D A2EN treated with D-PBS (mock infection controls) are depicted on the left. Infection with <em>Lactobacillus gasseri</em>, a health-associated cervicovaginal bacterium, is depicted on the right. 3D A2EN cervical cell aggregates treated with D-PBS or infected with <em>L. gasseri</em> were incubated for 24 hour under anaerobic conditions prior to processing for SEM imaging.</p></figcaption></figure></section></section></section><section id="S76"><h2 class="pmc_sec_title">
<em>SUPPORT PROTOCOL 7:</em> RNA extraction from 3D tissues</h2>
<p id="P606">These methods are optimized to extract total cellular (and viral) RNA from these 3D tissues (Basic Protocols 1 and 2). This RNA can be used to detect cellular and viral transcripts by qPCR (Basic Protocol 7) or used for transcriptomic analysis. Since the entire tissue is lysed, the gene expression profile will aggregate the different differentiated layers of tissue.</p>
<section id="S77"><h3 class="pmc_sec_title">Materials</h3>
<section id="S78"><h4 class="pmc_sec_title">Reagents, solutions, and cell lines</h4>
<ul id="L176" class="list" style="list-style-type:none">
<li>
<p id="P607">Frozen raft tissue (epidermal compartment) in 1.5 ml microcentrifuge tube (Basic Protocol 1)
</p>
<p id="P608">-OR-
</p>
<p id="P609">500 μl of aggregates in 1.5 ml microcentrifuge tube (Basic Protocol 2)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p id="P610">Forceps</p>
<p id="P611">Liquid nitrogen</p>
</li>
<li><p id="P612">RNeasy Mini Kit (Qiagen, cat. no. 74106)</p></li>
<li><p id="P613">Beta-mercaptoethanol</p></li>
<li><p id="P614">70% ethanol</p></li>
<li>
<p id="P615">1X Phosphate buffered saline (PBS)</p>
<p id="P616">TURBO DNA-free Kit (ThermoFisher Scientific, cat. no. AM1907)</p>
</li>
</ul></section><section id="S79"><h4 class="pmc_sec_title">Hardware and instruments</h4>
<ul id="L178" class="list" style="list-style-type:none">
<li><p id="P617">Pellet pestle (also referred to as a micro pestle)</p></li>
<li><p id="P618">Pipettors and pipet tips</p></li>
<li>
<p id="P619">Needles (20g, 25g) and syringes</p>
<p id="P620">QIAshredder columns (Qiagen, cat. no. 79656)</p>
<p id="P621">Microcentrifuge</p>
<p id="P622">Thermomixer or heat block (56°C)</p>
</li>
</ul></section></section><section id="S80"><h3 class="pmc_sec_title">Protocol steps</h3>
<ol id="L180" class="list" style="list-style-type:decimal">
<li><div class="p" id="P623">Mechanically disrupt 3D tissue
<ol id="L182" class="list" style="list-style-type:lower-alpha">
<li><div class="p" id="P624">
<strong>Organotypic raft tissue (Basic Protocol 1)</strong>
<ol id="L184" class="list" style="list-style-type:lower-roman">
<li><div class="p" id="P625">Carefully transfer liquid nitrogen to an appropriate container</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P626">Use forceps to hold and submerge the bottom of the 1.5 ml microcentrifuge tube (containing frozen tissue) in the liquid nitrogen.</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P627">Grind the tissue into a powder by rotating and moving a pre-cooled micro pestle up and down in the tube.</div></li>
<li>
<div class="p" id="P628">Ensure that the contents do not spill out and are kept frozen with liquid nitrogen (re-submerge the bottom of the tube as needed).
</div>
<div class="p" id="P629">It is important to ensure that the tissue is disrupted as quickly as possible while being kept cool, to avoid RNA degradation by RNases. Add lysis buffer as soon as the tissue is sufficiently disrupted (powder-like).</div>
</li>
</ol>
</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P630">
<strong>Rotating wall vessel tissue (Basic Protocol 2)</strong>
<ol id="L186" class="list" style="list-style-type:lower-roman">
<li><div class="p" id="P631">Wash tissue with 500 μl PBS</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P632">Add 200 μl PBS to the tissue</div></li>
<li>
<div class="p" id="P633">Homogenize tissue by passing it through a 20-gauge followed by a 25-gauge needle
</div>
<div class="p" id="P634">Critical. Do not transfer beads to the spin column (beads will clog column membrane resulting in low RNA yield)</div>
</li>
</ol>
</div></li>
</ol>
</div></li>
<li>
<p id="P635">Add 700 μl lysis buffer (containing 1 % beta-mercaptoethanol) from the RNeasy Mini Kit.
</p>
<p id="P636">Rinse the micro pestle and sides of the tube with this lysis buffer when using epithelial raft tissue mechanically disrupted by grinding.</p>
</li>
<li><div class="p" id="P637">Vortex the lysate for 10 sec.
<ol id="L1186" class="list" style="list-style-type:lower-alpha">
<li><div class="p" id="P638">Ensure complete homogenization.</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P639">If any tissue fragments are still visible then use a 20g followed by a 25g needle and syringe to further homogenize this mixture and aid lysis.</div></li>
</ol>
</div></li>
<li><p id="P640">Load 700 μl onto a QIAshredder column and centrifuge at maximum speed.</p></li>
<li>
<p id="P641">Follow the RNeasy Mini Kit procedure to bind, wash, and elute RNA.
</p>
<p id="P642">We elute with 50 μl pre-warmed (56°C) nuclease-free water.</p>
</li>
<li><p id="P643">Remove DNA from eluate using the Turbo-free DNase kit according to the manufacturer’s instructions.</p></li>
<li><p id="P644">Quantify the RNA concentration and purity spectrophotometrically.</p></li>
</ol>
<p id="P645">Proceed with reverse transcription immediately, keeping the RNA on ice, or store the RNA at −80°C. Avoid repeated freeze-thaw cycles as this could lead to degradation.</p></section></section><section id="S81"><h2 class="pmc_sec_title">
<em>BASIC PROTOCOL 7:</em> Characterization of gene expression by RT-qPCR</h2>
<p id="P646">The RNA isolated in <a href="#S44" class="usa-link">Support Protocol 6</a> can be used to detect cellular and viral transcripts by qPCR.</p>
<p id="P647">Here we provide an example to quantify the expression of HPV18 L1 mRNA. The L1 gene is expressed in differentiated cells, and is a marker for the switch to late viral gene expression and, presumably, virion assembly. Other viral and cellular genes can be quantified using different primer sets. The expression of many human ‘housekeeping’ genes changes throughout cellular differentiation (<a href="#R64" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R64">Steele et al., 2002</a>). We detect the human PPIA (Peptidyl-prolyl cis-trans isomerase A) gene as a reference.</p>
<p id="P648">Since the entire tissue is lysed, the gene expression profile will aggregate the different layers of tissue.</p>
<section id="S82"><h3 class="pmc_sec_title">Materials</h3>
<section id="S83"><h4 class="pmc_sec_title">Reagents, solutions, and cell lines</h4>
<ul id="L188" class="list" style="list-style-type:none">
<li>
<p id="P649">Cellular RNA extracted in <a href="#S76" class="usa-link">Support Protocol 7</a>
</p>
<p id="P650">SuperScript IV First-Strand Synthesis System (ThermoFisher Scientific, cat. no. 18091200)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p id="P651">Human reference gene (stable through differentiation, <a href="#R64" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R64">Steele et al., 2002</a>)
</p>
<p id="P652">PPIA, forward primer: 5’-AGAACTTCATCCTAAAGCATACGG-3’ (<a href="#R16" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R16">Dooley et al., 2016</a>)</p>
<p id="P653">PPIA, reverse primer: 5’-TGCTTGCCATCCAACCACTC-3’ (<a href="#R16" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R16">Dooley et al., 2016</a>)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p id="P654">Late viral life cycle marker
</p>
<p id="P655">HPV18 L1, forward primer: 5’-TAACACTACGCCTATAATACATTTAAAAGATG-3’</p>
<p id="P656">HPV18 L1, reverse primer: 5’-TACAACTCTTGCCACAGAAGGA-3’</p>
</li>
<li><p id="P657">Nuclease-free water</p></li>
<li><p id="P658">PowerUp SYBR Green Master Mix (ThermoFisher Scientific, cat. no. A25742)</p></li>
</ul></section><section id="S84"><h4 class="pmc_sec_title">Hardware and instruments</h4>
<ul id="L190" class="list" style="list-style-type:none">
<li><p id="P659">Pipettors and pipet tips</p></li>
<li>
<p id="P660">Needles (20g, 25g) and syringes</p>
<p id="P661">Thermomixer or heat block (56°C and 37°C)</p>
<p id="P662">1.5 ml microcentrifuge tubes</p>
<p id="P663">Mini-centrifuge with 200 μl PCR tube adapter</p>
<p id="P664">Thermocycler</p>
<p id="P665">Electronic pipettor (8-channel, 96 to 384-well adaptable)</p>
<p id="P666">384-well tips</p>
<p id="P667">Multichannel pipette reservoirs</p>
<p id="P668">384-well optical PCR plate</p>
</li>
<li><p id="P669">Sealable plate cover</p></li>
<li><p id="P670">Centrifuge with plate adaptor</p></li>
<li><p id="P671">Real-time thermocycler and computer with acquisition software</p></li>
</ul></section></section><section id="S85"><h3 class="pmc_sec_title">Protocol steps</h3>
<section id="S86"><h4 class="pmc_sec_title">Reverse transcribe RNA to cDNA</h4>
<ul id="L192" class="list" style="list-style-type:none">
<li>
<span class="label">1</span><div class="display-inline p" id="P672">Prepare reverse transcription reactions using the SuperScript IV First-Strand Synthesis System.
<ol id="L194" class="list" style="list-style-type:lower-alpha">
<li>
<div class="p" id="P673">Combine in 200 μl PCR tubes, for each annealing reaction.
</div>
<div class="p" id="P674">Make a master mix of the primer, dNTP, and water.
<ol id="L196" class="list" style="list-style-type:lower-roman">
<li><div class="p" id="P675">1 μl 50 μM Oligo d(T)<sub>20</sub> primer.</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P676">1 μl dNTP mix (10 mM each).</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P677">1 μg template RNA.</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P678">Make up to 13 μl with nuclease-free water.</div></li>
</ol>
</div>
</li>
<li><div class="p" id="P679">Flick to mix.</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P680">Briefly centrifuge.</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P681">Heat at 65°C for 5 min in the thermocycler.</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P682">Incubate on ice for at least 1 min while preparing the reverse transcription mix.</div></li>
<li>
<div class="p" id="P683">Combine in a separate 200 μl PCR tube.
</div>
<div class="p" id="P684">Make a master mix of these reagents when running multiple samples.
<ol id="L198" class="list" style="list-style-type:lower-roman">
<li>
<div class="p" id="P685">4 μl 5x SSIV buffer.
</div>
<div class="p" id="P686">Vortex and briefly centrifuge this buffer stock first.</div>
</li>
<li><div class="p" id="P687">1 μl 100 mM DTT.</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P688">1 μl Ribonuclease Inhibitor.</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P689">1 μl SuperScript IV Reverse Transcriptase (200 U/μl stock).</div></li>
</ol>
</div>
</li>
<li><div class="p" id="P690">Flick to mix.</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P691">Briefly centrifuge.</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P692">Add 7 μl of reverse transcription mix to the annealed RNA.</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P693">Incubate at 55°C for 10 min in the thermocycler.</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P694">Inactivate the enzyme by incubating at 80°C for 10 min in the thermocycler.</div></li>
</ol>
</div>
</li>
<li>
<span class="label">2</span><p class="display-inline" id="P695">Dilute the cDNA 10x by adding 180 μl nuclease-free water.</p>
</li>
<li>
<span class="label">3</span><p class="display-inline" id="P696">Keep the cDNA on ice if proceeding directly with qPCR, otherwise store at −20°C.</p>
</li>
</ul></section><section id="S87"><h4 class="pmc_sec_title">qPCR</h4>
<p id="P697">Plan your plate layout ahead of time, including all samples (with technical replicates), controls, and target wells.</p>
<ul id="L200" class="list" style="list-style-type:none">
<li>
<span class="label">4</span><div class="display-inline p" id="P698">Pre-mix forward and reverse primers for each target in 1.5 ml microcentrifuge tubes.
<ol id="L202" class="list" style="list-style-type:lower-alpha">
<li><div class="p" id="P699">Add 30 μl of 100 μM stock forward primer</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P700">Add 30 μl of 100 μM stock reverse primer</div></li>
<li>
<div class="p" id="P701">Top up to 1 ml with nuclease-free water
</div>
<div class="p" id="P702">This primer mix can be stored at −20°C and thawed for future use.</div>
</li>
</ol>
</div>
</li>
<li>
<span class="label">5</span><p class="display-inline" id="P703">Prepare separate target master mixes in 1.5 ml microcentrifuge tubes, for 10 μl reaction volume per well (7.5 μl of master mix per well) for each primer pair.
</p>
<div class="p" id="P704">
<em>Prepare enough master mix for technical triplicate of each sample and control, and 30% extra to account for pipette loss</em>.
<ol id="L204" class="list" style="list-style-type:lower-alpha">
<li><div class="p" id="P705">2 μl nuclease-free water.</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P706">0.5 μl primer mix.</div></li>
<li><div class="p" id="P707">5 μl PowerUp SYBR Green Master Mix.</div></li>
</ol>
</div>
</li>
<li>
<span class="label">6</span><p class="display-inline" id="P708">Mix by pipetting up/down 10x.</p>
</li>
<li>
<span class="label">7</span><p class="display-inline" id="P709">Dispense 7.5 μl mastermix to each well.</p>
</li>
<li>
<span class="label">8</span><p class="display-inline" id="P710">Dispense the template cDNA and controls (no-template control, water)</p>
</li>
<li>
<span class="label">9</span><p class="display-inline" id="P711">After the run, discard the plate and analyze the data using the ΔΔCt method (<a href="#R42" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R42">Livak &amp; Schmittgen, 2001</a>).</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p id="P712">Example RT-qPCR data are shown in <a href="#F8" class="usa-link">Fig. 8</a>.</p>
<figure class="fig xbox font-sm" id="F8"><h5 class="obj_head">Figure 8.</h5>
<p class="img-box line-height-none margin-x-neg-2 tablet:margin-x-0 text-center"><img class="graphic" src="https://cdn.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/blobs/3a7a/11088941/fb56f25def7b/nihms-1991549-f0008.jpg" loading="lazy" height="1920" width="1300" alt="Figure 8"></p>
<div class="p text-right font-secondary"><a href="figure/F8/" class="usa-link" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Open in a new tab</a></div>
<figcaption><p id="P792">Differentiation activates expression of the late viral genes. Expression of HPV18 L1 is quantified using RT-qPCR. HPV18 L1 (sliced transcript), in HPV18-infected human cervical keratinocyte 3D raft vs 2D monolayer culture. Fold change was calculated using the 2<sup>−ΔΔCt</sup> method, with HPV18 L1 relative to the human reference gene PPIA, and fold change calculated as 3D raft vs 2D monolayer culture.</p></figcaption></figure></section></section></section><section id="S88"><h2 class="pmc_sec_title">REAGENTS AND SOLUTIONS</h2>
<section id="S89"><h3 class="pmc_sec_title">50X TAE Buffer</h3>
<ul id="L206" class="list" style="list-style-type:none">
<li><p id="P713">50 mM EDTA disodium salt</p></li>
<li><p id="P714">2 M Tris</p></li>
<li><p id="P715">1 M glacial/acetic acid</p></li>
</ul></section><section id="S90"><h3 class="pmc_sec_title">Citrate buffer pH 6, 10 mM, 1 L</h3>
<ul id="L208" class="list" style="list-style-type:none">
<li><p id="P716">2.94 g sodium citrate dihydrate (MW = 294.1 g/mol)</p></li>
<li><p id="P717">Up to 1 L with autoclaved ddH<sub>2</sub>O</p></li>
<li><p id="P718">Adjust to pH 6 with NaOH</p></li>
<li><p id="P719">Store at room temperature, up to 3 months</p></li>
</ul></section><section id="S91"><h3 class="pmc_sec_title">Complete keratinocyte serum-free medium (KFSM) with 100 μg/ml Primocin</h3>
<ul id="L210" class="list" style="list-style-type:none">
<li><p id="P720">500 ml keratinocyte serum-free medium</p></li>
<li><p id="P721">Recombinant epidermal growth factor (supplied with medium)</p></li>
<li><p id="P722">Bovine pituitary extract (supplied with medium)</p></li>
<li><p id="P723">220 μl 100 mg/ml sterile CaCl<sub>2</sub> solution</p></li>
<li><p id="P724">1 ml Primocin, 50 mg/ml</p></li>
</ul></section><section id="S92"><h3 class="pmc_sec_title">Human fibroblast growth media, 500 ml (sterile)</h3>
<ul id="L212" class="list" style="list-style-type:none">
<li>
<p id="P725">DMEM (ThermoFisher Scientific, cat. no. 11960044)</p>
<p id="P726">10% fetal bovine serum (FBS)</p>
</li>
<li><p id="P727">100 U/ml penicillin/100 μg/ml streptomycin (ThermoFisher Scientific, cat. no. 15140122)</p></li>
<li><p id="P728">2 mM L-glutamine (Invitrogen #25030081)</p></li>
</ul></section><section id="S93"><h3 class="pmc_sec_title">Inactivation media, 500 ml (sterile)</h3>
<ul id="L214" class="list" style="list-style-type:none">
<li>
<p id="P729">DMEM (ThermoFisher Scientific, cat. no. 11960044)
</p>
<p id="P730">10% fetal bovine serum (FBS)</p>
</li>

</ul></section></section><section id="S100"><h2 class="pmc_sec_title">COMMENTARY</h2>
<section id="S101"><h3 class="pmc_sec_title">BACKGROUND INFORMATION</h3>
<p id="P772">The papillomavirus life cycle is intricately linked to the differentiation status of the infected tissue and cells. Therefore, the complex papillomavirus replicative cycle has been difficult to recapitulate in the laboratory. To decipher the fundamental biology of HPVs, it is essential to recapitulate the 3D structure of these tissues. Furthermore, epidemiological data strongly suggest that the nature of the infected tissue (i.e., cervix or tonsillar crypts) plays a critical role in how HPV interacts with the host (<a href="#R17" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R17">Doorbar &amp; Griffin, 2019</a>; <a href="#R58" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R58">Roberts et al., 2019</a>). This protocol provides complementary methods to establish 3D organotypic tissues representing cervical and oral epithelia. Unlike conventional monolayer cultures, both organotypic raft cultures and RWV-derived human 3D tissues recapitulate physiological architecture, such as apical and basal cell polarity, and ultrastructural features (<a href="#R2" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R2">Asselineau &amp; Prunieras, 1984</a>; <a href="#R36" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R36">Kopan et al., 1987</a>; <a href="#R54" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R54">Radtke et al., 2012</a>; <a href="#R54" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R54">Radtke &amp; Herbst-Kralovetz, 2012</a>).</p>
<p id="P773">Organotypic raft cultures (named due to the apparent floating nature of the cell-matrix) have been critical in deciphering different aspects of the HPV life cycle. These methods were initially developed to study skin biology and skin grafting research (<a href="#R5" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R5">Bell et al., 1983</a>; <a href="#R56" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R56">Rheinwald &amp; Green, 1975a</a>), and were later adapted to study HPV. The complete life cycle of a human papillomavirus (HPV) was first elucidated in this culture system (<a href="#R15" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R15">Dollard et al., 1992</a>; <a href="#R46" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R46">McCance et al., 1988</a>; <a href="#R48" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R48">Meyers et al., 1992</a>). In addition to the current protocol, other, excellent organotypic raft protocols have been published and used (<a href="#R1" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R1">Anacker &amp; Moody, 2012</a>; <a href="#R39" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R39">Lambert et al., 2005</a>; <a href="#R41" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R41">Lee et al., 2016</a>; <a href="#R53" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R53">Ozbun &amp; Patterson, 2014</a>; <a href="#R58" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R58">Roberts et al., 2019</a>). The ability to establish these 3D organotypic raft cultures from diverse human tissues will allow researchers to study how HPV (or other pathogens) interact with these physiologically relevant tissues. Indeed, we demonstrate that once isolated, these cells maintain properties reminiscent of the initial tissue.</p>
<p id="P774">The rotating wall vessel (RWV) bioreactor technology was developed by NASA in the 1990’s to study the impact of low fluid-shear modeled microgravity environment and this methodology was found to promote cellular differentiation and faithfully recapitulate features of human tissue (<a href="#R68" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R68">Unsworth &amp; Lelkes, 1998</a>). Cells are cultured with microcarrier beads providing an extracellular matrix for cells to attach within the low fluid-shear environment using RWV bioreactor thereby promoting cellular differentiation and formation of 3D tissue aggregates (<a href="#R24" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R24">Gardner &amp; Herbst-Kralovetz, 2016</a>). This culture methodology has been utilized to generate organotypic epithelial tissues from a wide variety of sites that recapitulate the <em>in vivo</em> architecture, barrier function, secretion of mucins, apical-basolateral polarity and transcriptional programs of <em>in vivo</em> tissue as reviewed extensively (<a href="#R4" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R4">Barrila et al., 2010</a>; <a href="#R24" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R24">Gardner &amp; Herbst-Kralovetz, 2016</a>). Furthermore, the 3D RWV-derived organotypic tissues have also been utilized to study a plethora of host-microbe interactions, including throughout the female reproductive tract (<a href="#R4" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R4">Barrila et al., 2010</a>, <a href="#R3" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R3">2018</a>; <a href="#R13" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R13">Crabbé et al., 2017</a>; <a href="#R18" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R18">Drummond et al., 2016</a>; <a href="#R24" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R24">Gardner &amp; Herbst-Kralovetz, 2016</a>, <a href="#R25" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R25">2018</a>; <a href="#R27" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R27">Herbst-Kralovetz et al., 2016</a>; <a href="#R32" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R32">Ilhan et al., 2020</a>; <a href="#R40" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R40">Łaniewski et al., 2017</a>; <a href="#R52" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R52">Nickerson et al., 2001</a>; <a href="#R60" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R60">Sainz et al., 2009</a>). It is becoming increasingly clear that 3D RVW-derived organoids provide researchers with advanced <em>in vitro</em> model systems that better resemble human <em>in vivo</em> tissue equivalents and are desirable when suitable animal models of infection are lacking or to complement other existing model systems.</p>
<p id="P775">There is currently no animal model that adequately mimics the human <em>Lactobacillus-</em>dominated cervicovaginal microenvironment (<a href="#R27" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R27">Herbst-Kralovetz et al., 2016</a>; <a href="#R72" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R72">Witkin &amp; Ledger, 2012</a>). Human cervical and vaginal lines derived from explanted tissues suffer from a finite life span and conventional 2D monolayer cultures fail to exhibit features of their parental <em>in vivo</em> tissue. The 3D RWV-derived A2EN cervical cells, on the other hand, faithfully recapitulate cellular phenotypes of <em>in vivo</em> tissue, such as apical and basal cellular polarity, microvilli, mucin secretion, and intracellular tight junctions (<a href="#R55" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R55">Radtke et al., 2012</a>; <a href="#R54" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R54">Radtke &amp; Herbst-Kralovetz, 2012</a>). Human A2EN cervical cells are immortalized by stable transfection with the HPV E6 and E7 proteins, therefore providing long-term replicative capacity (<a href="#R28" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R28">Herbst-Kralovetz et al., 2008</a>). Additionally, 3D A2EN cervical models have been colonized effectively with <em>Lactobacillus</em> spp. and bacterial vaginosis-associated bacteria, exposed to microbial products and challenged with pathogens and found to recapitulate clinical features of the cervicovaginal microenvironment (<a href="#R26" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R26">Gardner et al., 2020</a>; <a href="#R47" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R47">McGowin et al., 2013</a>; <a href="#R55" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R55">Radtke et al., 2012</a>; <a href="#R71" class="usa-link" aria-describedby="R71">Winkle et al., 2016</a>). Therefore, 3D RWV-derived cervical cell models described in these protocols may allow researchers to study how genital bacteria and pathogens of the cervicovaginal microenvironment influence the HPV lifecycle.</p>
<p id="P776">In conclusion, we provide detailed protocols on establishing and analyzing 3D tissues to study the interactions between HPV and its specific host tissues.</p></section><section id="S102"><h3 class="pmc_sec_title">CRITICAL PARAMETERS</h3>
<p id="P777">A successful 3D organotypic raft culture experiment requires healthy, proliferative cells. Furthermore, it is critical that researchers adhere to the stepwise process of building and lifting the rafts. Finally, these raft tissues are fragile, and careful handling throughout is essential. Both the fibroblasts and keratinocytes need to be viable to function properly for the duration of the raft procedure and should be proliferative without showing signs of senescence or transformation prior to initiating rafts. It is also critical that the appropriate media are used during each step of the procedure: EGF-containing F-media (with or without ROCK inhibition) when the basal keratinocytes are seeded. A switch to differentiation media (calcium-supplemented, without EGF and no ROCK inhibitor) is made once the tissues are lifted to the air-liquid interface. Each step of the raft process requires careful handling. When seeding the dermal equivalents you must work quickly, before the collagen-mixture solidifies, while avoiding the introduction of air bubbles. When lifting the rafts onto membranes you must take care not to break, drop, or place the cultures upside down.</p>
<p id="P778">With regard to the 3D RWV bioreactor-derived model system one should consider the initial set up cost of purchase the RWV bioreactor system (RLSS-4, power source, etc) and the time investment to generate fully differentiated 3D aggregates (28 days). The most critical parameters include the preparation of the beads and bioreactor, growth and health of the cells and appropriate seeding of the bioreactor. Additional parameters include close monitoring and maintenance of cells over the 28 day period. Bioreactors require media to be changed daily after a point in the protocol when the cells are consuming the nutrients as indicated by a color change in media. Following media changes, one must ensure that there are no bubbles in the bioreactor. These bubbles are removed carefully from the ports and the elimination of these bubbles are extremely important for aggregate formation. In addition, the rotation must be maintained 24 hours a day except for when changing the media. Failure to turn the rotator back, prior to differentiation and harvest, will result in a ruined batch of aggregates.</p></section><section id="S103"><h3 class="pmc_sec_title">TROUBLESHOOTING</h3>

</tr>

</tr>
<tr>
<td align="left" valign="top" rowspan="1" colspan="1"></td>
<td align="left" valign="top" rowspan="1" colspan="1">Loss of upper layers</td>
<td align="left" valign="top" rowspan="1" colspan="1">Handle rafts gently during harvest and processing to keep the stratified epithelia intact</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td align="left" valign="top" rowspan="1" colspan="1">Low 3D A2EN cervical cell aggregate yields</td>
<td align="left" valign="top" rowspan="1" colspan="1">Presence of air bubbles in the RWV bioreactor</td>
<td align="left" valign="top" rowspan="1" colspan="1">Completely remove bubbles from bioreactor after each feeding and on days when feeding is not required</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td align="left" valign="top" rowspan="1" colspan="1"></td>
<td align="left" valign="top" rowspan="1" colspan="1">Insufficient A2EN cells seeded into RWV bioreactor or low live cell yield</td>
<td align="left" valign="top" rowspan="1" colspan="1">Ensure the proper number of live A2EN cells (~1×10<sup>7</sup>) are obtained prior to seeding the bioreactor</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td align="left" valign="top" rowspan="1" colspan="1"></td>
<td align="left" valign="top" rowspan="1" colspan="1">STLV bioreactor was incubated without rotation immediately after seeding with the A2EN cells and microcarrier beads</td>
<td align="left" valign="top" rowspan="1" colspan="1">Ensure that the rotator power unit is powered on and set to 20 rpm immediately after seeding the STLV bioreactor with A2EN cells and microcarrier beads</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td align="left" valign="top" rowspan="1" colspan="1"></td>
<td align="left" valign="top" rowspan="1" colspan="1">Improper preparation of Cytodex-3 microcarrier beads</td>
<td align="left" valign="top" rowspan="1" colspan="1">Ensure that beads are soaked in sterile D-PBS overnight and autoclaved for the time and temperature specified in the protocol. Allow beads to cool to room temperature prior to mixing with A2EN cells.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td align="left" valign="top" rowspan="1" colspan="1">3D A2EN cervical cells develop into large clumps</td>
<td align="left" valign="top" rowspan="1" colspan="1">RWV rotating unit not powered back on to rotation during incubation or not set to the proper rpm</td>
<td align="left" valign="top" rowspan="1" colspan="1">Ensure that the RWV rotation is powered back on when replenishing media and that the rotating unit is working properly and set at 20 rpm during incubation</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table></div>

<p id="P781">This work was supported by a State of Arizona Improving Health TRIF to KVD. We are thankful to our colleagues for sharing materials and equipment. We are also grateful to past and present Van Doorslaer and Campos lab members for discussion during joint lab meetings, and in particular Kelly King for irradiating feeder fibroblasts used for primary keratinocyte culture as well as David Williams for preparing the HPV18-infected human cervical keratinocytes. We would like to acknowledge past and present Herbst-Kralovetz lab members for development and refinement of 3D RWV bioreactor protocols and downstream assays over the years. In addition, we are grateful for the generous gift of human A2EN cells from Dr. Alison Quayle (Louisiana State University Health Science Center).</p></section><section id="fn-group1" class="fn-group"><h2 class="pmc_sec_title">Footnotes</h2>
